"Oh, children, since I have completed for you this book, which is the last of the science of medicine, according to its perfection and conclusion, and through its explanations and statements, it seems to me that I complete it for you with this treatise on surgery."
"For the practice of surgery is much neglected in our region and time, such that it is almost lost to science, its traces are obscured; and there remain only a few small descriptions of it in the books of the Ancients, which are changed over time and lead astray those who follow them, because their intentions are unclear and the strength of this art is diminished."
"It seems to me that I should revive this (science) with an ordered treatise, in accordance with the method of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and that it should come accompanied by illustrations of cautery instruments and other tools used in surgery, for addition to the explanations and preparation of them, which is necessary."
"But the reason why there is no good practitioner of surgery in our time is because the art of medicine is extensive, and its practitioner must first be well-versed in the science of anatomy, which teaches the arrangement of the members and their shapes, their connections and separations; and have knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, their number and proportion; and of the pulsating veins and quiet ones, and the locations of their outlets."
"And therefore Hippocrates said that 'in name it is great, but in deed small,' especially in surgery."
"But as we have already said at the beginning of this book, whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have said regarding anatomy will surely fall into error, which causes many deaths among people, as I have seen happen too often, since some are formed in this science but depart from it without knowledge or experience."
"For I saw a foolish and inexperienced doctor accidentally cut an escrophilus tumor in the neck of a woman, and cut some arteries in her neck causing her to bleed profusely and die suddenly."
"And I saw another doctor who tried to remove a stone from the bladder of a man in whom it had formed, and while doing so he tore a piece of the bladder, causing that man to die on the third day."
"And I myself had already predicted that this would happen, and knew beforehand that he would die because of the size of the stone and the condition of the patient."
"And I saw another doctor who received payment from one of our dukes to practice surgery, and attempted to reset the thighbone of a black man who had suffered a fracture there. The doctor prepared himself with ignorance, reset the fracture on top of the joint without leaving room for breathing, using pillows and bolsters with great force."
"And he bound him up according to his desires, and applied poultices, and left him thus for several days commanding that he not be unbound. And so it was done until the thigh and knee became inflamed, and this resulted in destruction."
"And I was called to him, and prepared to remove the bandages, and thus tranquility was restored and he was freed from his pain."
"But nevertheless the corruption had already become established in the limb, so that I could not restrain it, and corruption continued to spread through the limb until the patient perished."
"And I saw another doctor who punctured a cancerous abscess and within a few days it became ulcerated and greatly worsened upon its lord."
"This is because the caustic humor of cancer is melancholic, and therefore it should not be treated with iron alone, but rather that part of the body which suffers from it should be cauterized."
"And therefore, my children, it is necessary for you to distinguish between two kinds of operations with the hand: one is an operation that brings about health, and another that involves danger in the greatest positions."
"And I have already mentioned this in every part of this book where operation is associated with error and danger; therefore it is necessary for you to guard against this and leave it alone, so that foolish people do not find a way to speak and dishonor you."
"And therefore take up your weapons with solicitude and protection from God, and approach illnesses with skillfulness and steadfastness."
"And follow the best way by the grace of God to obtain health and worthy success, and leave behind terrible illnesses that are difficult to cure, and wield your weapons against what causes you fear, so that your trust in your faith and in your name does not abandon you: for more remains to your glory, both here on earth and hereafter, and your sanctity."
"Because I have already discussed in some of my writings:" "No medicus medicine malae, ne malignos medicos nominem."
"And I have already divided this book into three parts."
"Beginning of the division of the book, and first of the first part." "The first chapter arranged concerning the head, regarding the forms of instruments and the irons for cauterization, and what is necessary in operation."
"The division of the second part." "The second chapter, concerning incision and perforation, cupping glasses, poultices, extraction of arrows and similar objects, all arranged according to the forms of instruments."
"The third chapter, concerning reduction and dislocation, and the cure of torsion and similar things; arranged according to the headings, regarding the forms of instruments."
"It is necessary for me to say what are the qualities of those who perform cauterization and those who receive it, and in what condition cauterization should be prohibited."
"Therefore I say that the discourse on the quality of the cauterizer and cauterized is long and prolix, subtle by science, and secret; many wise men have spoken about it, and they disagree among themselves, but for me to speak about all their discourses would be too lengthy."
"And therefore I say that cauterization is beneficial for all conditions universally, whether they have matter or not, except for two conditions, which are those without matter."
"In the condition that is dry and without matter, there is disagreement; for some said that cauterization is beneficial in this case, while others said the opposite, that cauterization is not suitable in an illness that is caused by quality and dryness, because fire has the qualities of heat and dryness, and it would not be appropriate for an illness that is dry and without matter to be healed with something that is hot and dry."
"And he says that which contradicts this, that cauterization is beneficial in all dry and hot diseases that occur in the bodies of men, for when you compare the body of man and its humidity to the composition of fire, you find the body of man cold."
"And I say by the speech of that one, that I have already experienced this many times."
"But it is not necessary that there come upon this that which has already been said and practiced in the chapter of cauterization by the last exercise, and to know the diversity of the composition of men and the disposition of diseases in their members, and the causes of these, and the accidents of them, and the space of time for those."
"But in other compositions there is no fear on you, and especially in hot and humid diseases, for all the physicians are agreed about those, and they are not disagreed in the judgment with cauterization in those."
"And know, son, that the secret of cure by cauterization with fire and its goodness is about cauterization with burning medicine, for fire is simple, whose action does not extend except to the member which is cauterized, and it does not reach another member joined with it without little harm."
"But the action of burning medicine extends to that which is near it in members, and often it brings disease into the member which is difficult to heal, and often it extinguishes."
"But fire, because of its sublimity and goodness of its substance, does nothing but superfluously. And it is already known to us by experiment and long service in studying the art about the truth of causes; and for that reason I am excused from lengthening my speech. But if it were not that it was not read in my book in this place to you secretly hidden with fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies and of its expulsion by which it expels diseases, with philosophical demonstration, which would serve to clarify your thoughts."
"And know, son, that they disagree about the time in which it is convenient to perform cauterization, and they consider the best time to be in spring."
"And I say that cauterization is convenient at all times, because the harm caused by the time of accident is submerged in the benefit of what is attracted by cauterization, and especially if the cauterization is for pains or necessary remedies for severe and chronic diseases, which cannot tolerate delay because it is feared that those may come to harm, which is greater than little harm entering through time."
"And also do not think, son, that only the common people and foolish physicians estimate this, for those diseases which are cured by cauterization are not always suitable at all times, and they consider that consequence."
"And the cause is not as they think for this reason, because cauterization is only in place of medicine which alters the complexion and dries up the moistures which are the cause of pains."
"But nevertheless, cauterization is superfluous on top of medicine because of the violence of its power and virtue of its operation and greatness of its lord."
"And it is possible that its disease returns at some hour of time, according to the complexion of the sick and the location of its disease, and the power of fire and what has been prepared in the body from the aggregation of superfluities in it, and what has been acquired by it in its acquisition through foods and similar causes; but the disease in which cauterization has been administered is a subtle disease in a member with few superfluities and moistures, thus as cauterization of the tooth for pain and similar to that one, it is possible that this pain does not return, but it happens rarely."
"And moreover common speech is that cauterization is the last remedy of medicine, and it is true speech, not because they understand in it what they think, for they believe that there is no cure that profits with medicine nor with any other cause before cauterization."
"And the cause is contrary to this; and the intention that cauterization is the last remedy of medicine is only when administering the methods of cure in certain diseases, and those medicines do not help, and therefore cauterization is administered at the end of the cause, and it profits there." "And from now on I say that cauterization is the last remedy of medicine, not according to the intention which common people and most foolish physicians understand."
"And they said in ancient times that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance."
"And they said that the place of cauterization does not matter, which is not absolutely true, because I have already proven and demonstrated that this does not happen except in some bodies without others, and cauterization with it is good and better than with iron as they said; but however when you perform cauterization with fire with gold, it is not declared to you, because it is ignited according to the quantity that you want due to the roughness of gold, and because it prepares to receive friction; and if you adjust it on ignition, the gold melts by the fire, and some sheets fall into the fire so that the artisan does not catch them by his occupation."
"And for this reason cauterization is performed with iron more lightly and more appropriately to the rectitude of operation."
"And I have already arranged this chapter on cauterization according to chapters, and have arranged those of the head within the weights, so that later requesting it you will find what you want from it."
The first chapter
This cauterization confers humidity and coldness upon the affected organ whose two causes are: its sodden nature and abundance of flux called catarrh, flowing from the head down to the eyes and ears, and causing sleepiness, toothache, sore throat, and universally all diseases that arise from coldness, such as paralysis, apoplexy, and similar afflictions.
The procedure for this cauterization is as follows: first, you should command the patient to be purged with a laxative medicine that clears the head, for three or four nights, depending on the severity of their illness, age, and usual habits.
And then you should command him to shave his head with a razor and perform that seat between your thighs on a padded bench, and let him place his feet upon his own chest.
And then you should place the palm of your hand close to the opening of his nose between his eyes. Yet nevertheless, when your hand has reached the middle of the wound, mark that spot with a thread, and then light the olive-oil cautery whose form is as follows:
Then place that upon the spot marked with thread, in such a manner that it descends slowly, so that your hand is gradually constrained, and you turn it around.
And then gently lift your hand up and look at the spot; if you see any of the bone now uncovered, about as much as the grain of an ergot, then lift your hand up again. If it does not return to its previous position with the iron, use another one until such time as you can see that which I have mentioned to you.
Then take a little salt and dissolve it over the spot and leave it for three days.
Then place it on the edge of the wound, folded in half, and leave it there until the fire's crust is destroyed. Then dress the wound with tetrafarmacon ointment until it is healed.

Burning for old migraine
When there is a sudden pain in the head, or it spreads into the ear, if medicines that relieve headaches are not effective and other treatments have been tried without success, then cauterization should be performed using either an acid cautery or a hot iron.
To perform cauterization with an acidic cautery, take a pennyworth of salt and dissolve it in vinegar. Then make an incision with a sharp scalpel at the location of the pain on the temple, so that it is hidden under the hair.
Next, press on the wound with a clean cloth for several hours to prevent bleeding. Then remove the cloth after three hours and wipe away any remaining salt. Leave the wound uncovered for two or three days until it heals completely.

"And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula which some first said: Enter into the location of the fistula and fill it with that subtle camphor of which it has the form; and melt in that amount of melted lead equal to one inch; then take your hand with careful retention, so that the melted lead does not reach the wound of the patient; and cover the spot on the skin where you inserted it with albumen of egg or water, because lead adheres to the location of the fistula and heals it through marvelous healing."
"And if the fistula is healed with what we have said about cauterization and treatment, that is good. But if not, then it is necessary to administer a tractive agent for the nose and reduce the fistula to the course of the nose according to what will come in its proper place."

"Chapter XIX."
"On the cauterization of fistula in the mouth."
"When an abscess appears in the uvula or palate or roots of teeth and it becomes inflamed, then bursts open, and becomes infected, and pus comes out and a fistula is formed, if you treat it and your treatment does not improve, then you should kindle cautery according to the amount received in the fistula, and melt that heated iron into the tract of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the heated iron reaches the depth of it, and repeat this once or twice; and then treat it with what we have said about treatment until it is healed."
"And then if the inflammation is cut off and it is healed, that is good. But if not, then it is necessary to discover the location and remove the rotted bone according to what will come in its chapter."
"Chapter XX."
"For cauterization of the teeth and softening of the veins."
"When veins are softened by humidity and teeth are painful, if you cure them with medicines without success, then place the patient's head on your thigh, and bring the cautery in this shape near, so that you place the cup over the tooth and quickly insert the cautery into it. Remove your hand a little bit so that the patient feels the heat of the fire reaching the root of the tooth."
"And then remove your hand, and repeat the cautery several times according to what you want."
"Then the patient should rinse their mouth with salt water and hold it for an hour, then spit it out, because the painful tooth is hardened and the softened gum is strengthened and the humidity is dried."
Chapter XX
**On Toothache Cauterization**
When toothache is caused by coldness or worm within, or medicine does not help the cure, then cauterize it with one of two methods: either cautery with cow's dung or cautery with fire.
To cauterize with cow's dung: Take some cow's dung and boil it in a pot of iron. Then take some cotton, wrap it around the tip of the toothpick, dip that into the boiled cow's dung, and quickly apply it to the painful tooth before it cools down.
And repeat this several times until the power of the fire reaches the root of the teeth.
And if you wish, dip some wool or cotton into the aforementioned cow's dung, place it on the painful tooth, and then quickly apply a red-hot iron onto it until the iron reaches the crown of the tooth's concavity.
But cauterizing with fire is that you wait for the coal or iron to become red-hot and glowing, and then carefully apply it onto the tooth without touching the inside of the mouth of the sick person.
And then shape the coal or iron as you wish and apply it to the tooth, keeping your hand away until it cools down. Repeat this several times until the pain is gone, either on that same day or the following day.
And it is necessary that after this cautery, the sick person keeps their mouth closed tightly on both sides and holds it like that for an hour, and then spits it out. This is the form of cautery.
And cauterize in whatever way you wish, according to what you are capable of doing.
And this is how the cautery should be performed:

And if the swelling is small, then pause the cautery according to its quantity, and leave it for three days, pausing over the wound's edge until what the fire has burned is removed.
Then dress that wound with ointments, bandages, and cloths until it heals.

"Chapter XXVII."

"And if it is in the tunic of the liver, then the pain will be sharp and intense, and sometimes the physicians are tired from its treatment."

But if you cauterize with a large cautery over several [haemorrhoids], it will cause more harm than good.

Then heat the cautery which resembles a needle-red-hot. And then insert that heated cautery into this fistula, going in as far as the probe entered.

"And afterwards dress the wound so that it may heal."

Chapter XL.
Of the cauterization of the sciatic vein.
When pain arises from the opening of a hernia, and its cause is friction and moisture, the patient is cured with what we have said earlier and not otherwise, then you must release the patient from thick humors with pills made from fetid or artificial substances or similar ones; and then cauterize that part.
And the method of cauterizing that part is done in two ways: either with cauteries using burning medicines or with fire.
Choose one of two known methods: the first is to cauterize that part over the opening of the hernia with three triangular cauteries in this shape, and make them of good depth. And let the space between each cautery be equal to the thickness of a finger, if the cauteries are olive-sized or larger.
But sometimes it may happen that the cauteries are placed over the middle point above the head of the hernia, so there will be four cauteries.
And if you wish, you can cauterize with a circle whose shape is the same as in the cauterization of dislocation of a hernia. Let it be a continuous circle that burns the heat of all the cord.
And this is the method of cauterizing sciatica when pain adheres to the hernia and does not extend into the groin.
But if it extends into the groin, then cauterize that area with two cauteries over the groin above the point where you feel the pain; and one cautery over the knee, about four fingers' breadth down from the left side of that part.
And if using a cautery knife, let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the cord.
And if the pain extends to the area near the left groin, then cauterize there where you feel it with three or four cauteries or more as needed.
And if the pain seems to be beneath the groin, then cauterize that area with one cautery knife.
And be careful in all cauterizations not to end with the cautery burning nerves or large arteries, lest you cause harm or contraction to the affected part.
And I have seen some of those who cauterized over the knee and ended up injuring nerves during the procedure, causing the leg to swell, with tumors reaching up to the thigh. The flesh became inflamed, putrefied, and the whole leg was corrupted. And thus happens a frequent complication of abdominal surgery, often leading to death.
If the pain is in two parts at once, cauterize each one separately according to this method.
The wise have said in the cauterization of hernia that the cautery should be shaped like an iron ring whose circumference is about that of a handspan. And let it be placed somewhat down from its own opening, according to the thickness of a finger bone or less.
And within that circle let there be another third one; and let the space between them be equal to the thickness of a pulse; and let those circles be open at two parts; and let their length be about one or two pulses, and make in those edges decently sharpened iron margins within the circles. This is its shape:
"A large fire should be kindled until it glows and sparks, then placed over the patient's buttocks, with the patient lying on their side." "And therefore cauterize that area three times in one visit."
"And so leave it alone for three days; plaster that area with a border and let the wound remain open too long; and treat that area with egg whites until it is healed."
"Son of mine, regarding this type of cauterization, we have not used it much because of the fear of causing injury to it, and because few cases have been found where it is applied."

Then press those below gently but firmly with your hand and leave the hole that allows the sharp water to pass through from the earthenware pot into the inverted pot."

"Chapter 45."
"On cauterization of fractures."
"When there is a fracture in the ankles or shins causing swelling before the thigh at the beginning of the injury, then you should order the patient to abstain from food on that day and use gentle laxatives so that the swelling in his abdomen may subside."

"And then ignite the cautery which is made in this shape:"
Within there may be much heat and throwing of sparks. Then carefully reduce the intestine or hernia to its cavity, and place your hand over it so that it does not slip out.

Then place the cautery on that same sign with your right hand, and push this intestine with the tip of the knife into the middle of the abdomen; repeat this procedure again if you have not yet succeeded in doing so.
And carefully observe the sensation of the intestine during your cauterization, so that you do not burn it and cause harm to the patient or bring about death.
Know that if with the cautery you do not seize the intestine, your operation will be futile.
And it is necessary that the cautery for children be thin according to their size and proportion.
Then take care of the burn wound for three days by applying a compress with clean water so that it may heal quickly.
And then treat him with other remedies until he is healed.
And the patient should remain in bed for forty days until the wound and inflammation are sealed.
It is necessary that the patient's nutrition be restricted according to the length of time for his healing, so that the intestines do not prolapse due to the effort of recovering.
And when it is time to get up after about forty days, then administer food gradually and carefully, keeping him in bed for another forty days.
And he should be spared from work and excessive eating and drinking, and loud talking, for if one uses this method of healing entirely without moderation, it will not bring about a cure.
And now I will discuss the treatment of ruptures in other parts of the abdomen, and if it happens that they are not detected immediately, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size, and apply water as has been said. And treat him with the same care as mentioned above.
And some early writers have said that a rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery in this shape, for it is marked with an indentation:
"And it is placed a line that goes for the width on the side above the rupture, and another line above; then place your hand with a pointed cautery, but the first cautery should be lighter and better."
"Chapter Forty-six."
"On cauterizing a hemorrhoid."
When pain occurs in the limbs due to congestion or percussion and persists for a long time without being relieved by medical treatment, then it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And let the cautery be applied to every limb according to its size and smallness, strength and weakness, location of the twist and intensity of pain.
Therefore if the first cautery heals it, that is good. But if not, then repeat the cautery; for it is customary with those pains to be punctured in the limb that approaches the affected area, so that you must reach those with the cautery until the illness is healed.
Chapter XLVI
Of the cauterization of leprosy.
Some people view leprosy as benefited by cautery, but there is little improvement if the species of leprosy is caused by putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
And therefore, when you want to cauterize that person, consider whether the leprosy is contagious and treat it according to what has been said in its division. Do not delay if this is present, and fear that corruption will spread throughout the whole body and entire complexion of the patient. Then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head, another near it towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and both on the two horns; and one behind, on the nape or servant's mark.
And lastly, press the cauteries slightly into the bone to leave a small impression and remove the scabs, so that the expiration of thick vapors is alleviated from it. And cauterize on the chest as necessary.
And if the leprosy has already spread over the patient and appears manifestly, then you should cauterize him with those cauteries which we have said in the head; and cauterize on the tip of the nose, and with two cauteries on each cheekbone, and two cauteries on each shoulder blade of the neck, and six cauteries on each shoulder blade of the back, and one large one over the shoulder blades near the nape, and one over the nape itself, and two over the ankles, and one over each ankle, and two over the knees and one over each knee, and two over the elbows, and two over the wrists; and cauterize him over all the joints of those limbs and feet, and over each heel of his feet, and over the fleshy parts of his legs.
And beware of the nerves which are on the heel that you do not burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with one cautery on the bone of the breastbone and another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the liver.
And know that the more closely you apply cauteries, the greater is the benefit and efficacy. And know that the patient feels no pain from the cautery, as they do with their own sores, because the body of the sufferer has become numb.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be large or small according to the limbs and joints as specified in the descriptions of the instruments.
And afterwards, cure the cautery with powdered earth mixed with honey, and with the other remedy until it is healed.
Capítulo .xlviii.
Chapter XLVIII: Cauterization for Stupor
When any limb is paralyzed or asleep and is treated with medications, oils, and poultices, but does not heal, then you should cauterize that paralyzed limb with cauteries according to the size of the limb or its smallness.
And let your cautery enter a little into the thickness of the flesh And afterwards, cure it with ointment until it is healed.
And sometimes it is cauterized some paralysis which extends to the arms and legs, and to the shoulder blades of the back and through the movement of the nerves which cause that limb to be paralyzed, and the paralysis is removed.
But let not anyone presume to do this except one who is skilled in the anatomy of limbs and the exit of nerves throughout the whole body that moves.
Capítulo .xlix.
Chapter XLIX: Cauterization for Morphea (scleroderma)
When morphea is old and does not respond to any medicinal ointments, then you should cauterize it with a hot cautery a little according to the quantity of the thickness of the flesh until the whiteness and color are removed and its color is changed.
And afterwards, cure it with powdered earth and lentils mixed with olive oil and with leaves of mallows, and with pigeon blood or hen blood, giving each one part and mixing them all together, and afterwards a cloth should be placed on it and left to rest until it is healed.
Capítulo L.
Chapter L: Cauterization for Cancer
When cancer begins and you wish to remove it, then cauterize it with a round cautery around its circumference just as it is encircled.
And the wise ones said that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle of it. But I have not seen this, because I fear that it might become ulcerated, and I have seen this happen sometimes.
It is more fitting that it be cauterized around its circumference using such a circle as we have described, or with several cauteries.

Chapter four
Of the treatment of acute and acidic tears in the eyes
When there are acidic tears, it is the body of those veins that are above the head's crown that are affected, and no medical cause can be found for this condition. Sometimes the patient's face becomes reddened, and they feel a crawling sensation on their forehead as if ants were walking there. The eyes become weakened and watery to the point where the eyelashes stick together, and the skin around them becomes rough due to the acidity of the tears. The ancient remedy for this condition is as follows, and it should be applied without delay:
"I command the patient to raise their eyebrows that are on their forehead and then incise three equal furrows there according to the length of the forehead." "And if the length of the furrow is two fingers: let one furrow be equally distant from the length of the nose in the middle of the forehead, and the second according to the length slightly below the movement of the muscles that are in the lacrimal, and the third on the other side."
"And beware of the incision of the arteries that are on both sides, and extend your hand from the continuation of both jaws." "And if the space of each incision is the amount of three fingers placed together."
If you have on hand a sponge prepared with dry cloths to absorb blood.
And then insert the spatula of two pointed extremities, which is shaped like this: which should be placed between the temples towards the second incision. Remove with that all the chain which is between two incisions and place it above the bone, then do this from the middle incision to the second incision. Then insert into this spatula and place it into the first incision again with another instrument called a scalpel which is sharp on one side and not sharp on the other.
And cut with that sharp side next to the attached flesh near the chain, and also cut on the inner side of the bone, then employ it so that it reaches the middle fissure, and cut with it all the vessels that descend from the head to the heels.
But make sure that the incision continues until you can see the chain, and then do this in the middle fissure towards the other fissure.
And since some blood may have flowed out, express the places where the blood clots are located.
Then press in each fissure carefully with cotton wool, and apply those powders mixed in wine and oil and vinegar to prevent the formation of pus.
And on the third day untie the ligament and administer a large infusion of cold water or tea. Then cure it with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil and other remedies so that the wounds are healed.
Capítulo V
Regarding the treatment of injuries caused by cuts and the descent of parts from inside the head.
When someone suffers from cuts that are sharp and continuous, and sometimes the eyelids of the sick person appear thin and pale, and their gaze is weakened, and the eyelids become ulcerated and in their case the hair falls out, and there is acute painful sensation in the forehead followed by excessive sweating, then you should know that these materials and cuts do not come from outside but from small veins that originate from inside.
And the best treatment for these cases is this: command the sick person to raise their forehead, and then cut a fissure in that middle point of the forehead about half an inch wide (starting from the left temple towards the right temple; and the incision should be between the bones; and remove your hand from the temples' muscles which are attached due to mastication), until the bone is exposed.
Dry all the blood with a sponge or with dry cloth and then fill between the two lips of the fissure with cotton wool or with linen. Then press down from above with powders mixed in wine and oil to prevent the formation of pus.
And when you untie it and see that the pus has diminished, then it is necessary to scrape the bone where it begins to have flesh, and then cure it with a drying regimen which causes the flesh to emerge, as if you take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony and mix them together to make a plaster and apply it to these wounds until the fresh flesh appears.
Capítulo VI
Regarding the treatment of cuts on the ears.
There are four causes of cuts on the ears: either it is due to a mineral point like stone, or something similar such as iron and bronze, or it is due to plants such as thorns or beans, or it is due to a flowing cause such as water and vinegar and things like them, or some animal.
And when a stone cut the ear or some other similar cause that does not fit well in the ear and causes pain, then place the ear in the sun, and if it is sharp, then distill into that cause some violet oil or safflower oil, and apply the extract of it, and make them sneeze with some condiment, and plug their nose during the arrival of the sneezing. And then place on the circumference of the ear some pieces of cloth or wool, and stretch the ear upwards at its parts because very often it is forgotten with these causes.
And if it is not removed, then apply the extract of it using the instrument called "gesti epicicarious subtile" which has this form:
"If a birth has been forgotten in motion, it's well. If not, then administer extraction with a subtle hook of little duplication."
"And thus if it has not been forgotten because of that, then make a cannula of silver and insert its tip into the tear of the eardrum, closing around the cannula with wax and softened oil so that nothing gets in except for the cannula." "And then extract [the fetus] with a small windlass with strong attraction, because many have seen this that we have spoken about."
"But if it has not been forgotten in this manner, then take hot pitch or sometimes prepared wax with which the ears are taken a small amount, and pause that on the tip of the arrow, and then wrap it around that gently paused spot." "And then insert that into the tear of the ear with ease, and also remove the ear from its moisture."
"And therefore if it has not been forgotten in all the causes that we have spoken about, then you should cut off that before it becomes an abscess or spasm."
"And the way to cut off that is that you first sanctify the patient with the vein of the head and extract the blood according to its strength, and then make that cheese between your hands and convert the ear to the parts of it, and finish with a small incision in the root of the ear where there is pressure from it." "And let the incision be in the shape of a crescent moon that reaches to the stone, and when the stone is hardened, remove it if you can with appropriate instruments, and then close up the incision at that time with haste, and cure it until it is healed."
"And if the cause of the pain in the ear is one of the hairs that are growing and swollen, then administer the cure and extraction of it. But if it does not obey your efforts, then you should take a fine pointed probe in this shape:" "I will administer to him the removal of that stone which has fallen into his ear."
"And do not do this if you think that the stone has already been moistened by earwax, and pause for a moment, removing it with tweezers or some subtle gesture, or using an incision as described above, because removal will be easier."
"Put water into the ear from which the patient suffers from sneezing at the beginning, and fill their ear with a small piece of cotton wool, and place your finger over that ear into which the water has entered. "Then cease this until all the water has been expelled."
"Then cease this until all the water has been expelled." "And if the water is not expelled in this way, then take some paper or cotton wool, and put one end of it into the ear and extend the other end towards the fire until it catches light."
"And then put in another piece of cotton wool and do this as many times as necessary until all the water is expelled, and afterwards squeeze it out with a syringe as mentioned above regarding the stone extractor."
"If something enters the ear, if it is a small object, then do as I have said above regarding pushing it out. But if it is a large object which causes pain in the area of the cheekbone, then extract it with hooks and forceps. The cause of this is usually easier to remove than all other causes that occur in the ear."

"Chapter VII."
"Of the treatment of blockage of ears."
Some children sometimes exit from the wombs of their mothers unperforated, and this has happened in some men, opacity in the middle of the ear due to phlegm or flesh undigested in that place; and this opacity is sometimes formed in the front of the opening of the ear which does not hinder sight, and sometimes it is on the outside parts.
And that which happens in its front, which does not comprehend sight, is among the most difficult conditions to heal.
And regarding that one where sight succeeds, it is necessary that you hold the sick person's ear towards the sun and look at that. And thus if sometimes opacity appears, open that with a subtle spatula of which this is its shape:
If the end of it where its width is small, one part is sharp and the other is not; and the spatula should be of two lion's teeth to prevent injury to the ear.
And thus if the opacity is due to flesh born in the ear or in its membrane, then use those with subtle forceps and cut that violently until all the flesh is removed.
And if opacity is in front of the ear, then take a subtle lion's hair and heat it with fire a little, and put that into the membrane of the ear.
And thus if there is opacity with what the sick person finds easy, due to gravity of hearing, forcefully remove that oppression with ease; and make sure not to damage the nerves of the ear.
And then place the ear drop made of it according to the quantity of the width of the tract which you have wrapped in Egyptian ointment; and do this for several days until you are sure of the healing of the wound; or else take any wax and insert that into water and pulverize it over it three times and use it; and if sometimes the ear is already inflamed, then it is necessary that you cut the wax and replace it with another wax which you will wrap in cerot made with crushed rose oil until the inflammation has been cauterized; and then treat it until it is healed.
But if bleeding occurs, then immerse a sponge or cloth in hot water and place it over the ear, and use the other treatment which restricts blood flow, which is described in the treatise on distillation.
Chapter VIII
Of the Treatment of Swelling Which Occurs on the Eyelids.
"Those who have experienced some moisture on their eyelids occasionally are sometimes dry-eyed."
"Therefore you should have those [servants] ready with towels or cloths, and untie those [servants'] aprons from their waists, and carefully pause over the area as described."
"If pain comes with blood flow, then cauterize it with a fine silver-hot cautery."
"And the best cauterization is close to incisions and wounds that repeatedly return when there remains some cause of their weeping; and when they are cauterized with fire, those causes are burnt up and do not return."
"Chapter Nine."
"Treatment for swelling that comes to the eyelids."
"Many times it happens that in the eyelids there is some cause that resembles hardness and toughness, and for this reason it is called swelling."
"And it is an accumulation of thick humidity in the left eyelid above."
"Therefore, the operation in their case is that if the swelling appears on the outside of the eyelid and extends all around; its cause is light."
"Therefore, cut over that [swelling] with a transverse incision, and carefully explore around it with ease; and suspense it with pressure and cut off that [swelling]."
"And if its size is large, then adjust it with suturing; and cure it until it is healed."
"And if it is small, you will not suffer harm from that because the ointment for it restores it and heals it."
"And if the swelling leans towards the inside of the eyelid below the surface, then raise up the eyelid and suspense the swelling with pressure, except that you do not need to make an incision; and press it all around; and if the eyelid is lengthened by incision, then know there is no cause."
"And when you make the incision, wash the eye with salt water; and cure that place with what heals until it is healed."
"Chapter X."
"Of the treatment of swelling above the eyelid."
"Swelling is a growth that occurs in the tissues of the eyelid above, and especially in children, it aggravates their eyes and affects their sight greatly; and they cannot look at the brightness of the sun because tears flow down to them."
"And therefore they constantly have to keep their heads elevated and sleep with their heads raised; and because of this the eyelids of their left eyes become wet and inflamed, and there is already a threat of swelling apparent in the eye; and when you press that place with your fingers, you feel heat within them."
"And there is some way of operating in that case where the illness causes him to hold his head tilted back with his chin raised up and covered with a cloth; and make a circle around it according to its size, and place that on it and press with your fingers all around until swelling is gathered together in the middle of the circle; and then cut through the middle of that humidity with a spatula incision made transverse, and let the incision not be greater than the incision that is made in trepanation."
"But beforehand cover that you cut through the entire cord until you reach the swelling, because in most cases it proceeds through a fissure according to its form of whitish hardness."
"Therefore extract it with cloths which you have wrapped between your fingers at the outer parts and roll them between your right and left hand until it is completely gone."
"And be sure that you do not adjust in the incision lest with the spatula you reach the eye and damage it."
"But if no swelling appears at the beginning of the incision, then adjust it slightly with ease until swelling proceeds; and then extract it as we have said; and then apply cloths dipped in wine and vinegar to that place and cover it with powders."
"And there are some who throw salt onto it and cover it up in the concavity of the incision so that what remains of that humidity."
"And then cure it until it is healed."
"But if an abscess occurs in the place after, then cure it with cataplasms of Cedar until it is healed."
"Chapter XI."
"Of methods for examining the eye."
"When the eyelids of the eyes are born with adjusted left eyelashes and overgrown eyebrows, then they do not allow light to reach the eye and cause ways of illness such as continuous tears and inflammation of the eyelids and skin, which could be the cause of destruction of the eye that is called 'tactinir' of the eye, and it is cured in four ways: either by cautery with fire; or with acute medicine according to what has been said earlier in the chapter on cautery; or it is done by tactinir through incision and suturing; or by canthotomy as I will say."
"And therefore you should hold the head of the ill person tilted back; then turn the eyelid of the eye with your left hand, and if it is turned, that's good; but if not, insert a needle into that one in which there is fat near the outer edge of the eyelid, and make the needle penetrate through the fat above, and close to the edge of the eyelid where the hairs are located, and pull the thread up with the eyelid folded back using tweezers."
"And then make an incision in the area inside the eyelid near the adjusted hairs with a spatula incision from the greater lacrimal duct into the lesser lacrimal duct; and then extract the thread and put powdered small bits of cotton or cloth under the eyelid, and sew it back together with needle and thread, so that it resembles the shape of a myrtle leaf."
"But nevertheless the shape should be according to the amount of elevation of the eyelid, because that is already diversified in people, since some require a greater incision of the eyelid according to how much it has become inflamed."
"And then make an incision with the spatula along the two lines which you have sewn together, starting from the greater lacrimal duct and going into the lesser lacrimal duct." "And if your incision is close to the natural hairs like the thickness of a barleycorn."
"And then place a clamp on one of the two angles of the cord and then excoriate it completely, and then approximate the two lips with stitches using gut or thin thread of wool, and remove the blood, and make what is superfluous from the threads adhere to both eyebrows with some adhesive agent if you wish to do so, otherwise don't bother."
"And then leave the stitches for three or four days, and then dress it."
"And if you wish, leave the plaster without stitches and dress it with something that dries and constricts, because the eyelid is raised due to the sealing of the plaster and the adhesion of glue; but stitching is better. And this is what the ancients said about taxanir."
"But nevertheless, if there is solicitude over the illness and it is of good operation, then fear should not be present in him."
"And there is another manner in taxanir, which is to sew the eyelid with stitches resembling a myrtle leaf shape, and then lift the eyelid using three separated and gathered threads according to this form:"
"If this is not possible, hold the eyelids open, and if they do not stay open, then take a needle with thread attached and insert it into the center of the eye socket. Insert another thread near the larger lacrimal gland, and a second thread near the smaller one, adjust these threads evenly between your fingers, and raise your hand slightly upward to lift up the entire eyelid."
"And next, adjust both lips of the wound with stitches, and dress the area that is healing."
"If an abscess appears around your incision or wound, drain it with cerote and clean the surrounding area thoroughly."
"And sometimes the eyelid margin turns inward, in which case you should use the technique mentioned earlier for incision; but stitching is usually more effective."
"The procedure for cauterization with hot irons is as follows:" "And if you wish to cauterize the eyelid margin, first turn it inward and then incise along the line indicated earlier; next, prepare two thin wires or rods whose length is equal to that of the eyelid margin and whose width is less than that of a needle." "And once you have incised both ends of each cut, grasp the threads with your forceps."
"Apply each with subtlety beneath this which superfluously flows from the eyelid of the eye, and compress the tubes of each divided part with strong constriction, leaving it so for several days, because the conduit will die and be denied due to the constriction, and it can enter until such time that it falls by itself."
"If it is delayed, break the thread with the tweezers, and immediately cure the ulcer until it is healed."
"Once it has hardened, elevate the eyelid and the hairs will not pinch."
"And this is the form of two tubes which you shall make according to this form:" "and have the quantity of length and width neither more nor less."
Chapter XII
"Regarding the elevation of painful hairs in the eye with a needle when the hair is hard."
"When hairs are unnatural, hard, rough and painful to the eye, then the operation in this case is that you take a subtle needle and place it on that thread of fine silk and lion's hair, and carefully adjust its ends so that it does not hurt." "And let the length of the threads be of the quantity of a palm."
"Then take another subtle thread and tie it below it, and knot its ends if you wish."
"And then place the patient's head on a pillow facing the sun so that your work is illuminated, for this is subtle and delicate surgery."
"And then insert the needle into the root of the hair that needs to be removed, and make it penetrate into the eyelid quickly until you extract it from above the natural hair."
"And then pull out the hair from above and insert that one in its place; let there be one or two or three hairs, but no more than that."
"And then remove your hand with the hair so that it is completely outside of the eyelid along with the natural hair."
"But if the hair is pulled out along with it and the pellet is not removed, you will pull it again on both sides with the thread that you have prepared with it until the pellet comes out from underneath."
"And then close it with the vision of the eye, for then you will remove both the hair and the thread, wipe carefully and close the eyelid, and leave it like that for two or three days until the hair adheres to its place and grows back good flesh."
"And if the hair is too short, then you adjust a long natural hair and lift it with that one; or let it remain until it grows out about some space, and then you lift it."
Chapter XIII
On the treatment of twitching that occurs on top of the eyelid.
When twitching occurs in the eyelid, it is a contraction of the eyelid when it contracts on top, either to the right or left side, due to bad consolidation of plague, section, or cauterization; and this twitching is called "leporina," and this twitching can be natural or accidental, and it is caused by consolidation of plague, sections, or cauterizations, or by resembling those who are afflicted.
The method of the operation for this is that you should cut open that consolidation and separate the lips of it, and place in it a wick of linen cloth dipped in water, and tie those up until they are healed.
And it is not necessary that you use any cure for this that dries or constricts it, because if you do so, it will return to twitching worse than ever before.
Use on it causes that soften it like fenugreek, and soak it with the water in which it is cooked and sown, or with diachylon ointment, which has been liquefied with some of its oils, and dip the wick in that, and cure it with that.
And the treasure of your cure is that you should perforate with everything that is not consolidated according to the form that it had at the beginning.
And this operation that we have spoken of is nothing but some correction of twitching that does not return to its original form again.
Chapter XIV
"Concerning the treatment of blepharitis occurring in the eyelid."
"This blepharitis, which occurs on the left eyelid, is properly called blepharitis. It may be either congenital or acquired."
"Acquired blepharitis is caused by inflammation or injury or burning or other similar conditions."
"The procedure for performing this operation is as follows: Take a needle with doubled thread and insert it into the flesh, then pass it from the left lachrymal duct to the right, so that the thread reaches both ends of the flesh."
"And then extend the flesh at its two ends using the needle and cauterize it with the hot needle, then cut it open with a wide spatula." "And then if the eyelid returns to its normal shape, that is good. But if not, take a splint and place it in the slit of the eyelid, and with that turn the eyelid back into position, and suture the two wounds on the inner side of the left eyelid."
"And if the ends of the two wounds are at two corners of the incision, then make sure that they meet, and that their angle is such that when they come together they form a straight line."
"And this shape is called the Greek letter lambda (λ)."
"And then remove that flesh on the amount that is equal to the thickness of the eyelid on its inner side."
"And then approximate the separated parts and suture them with linen thread; and then dress it using the moistening medicines and compresses that we have mentioned, until it is healed."
"And if there are any recurrences later due to a wound, suture or cautery, then it is necessary that you make an incision with a flat blade on the skin of the eyelid according to what has been described above." "And then separate with a compress between the two lips according to what we have said."
"In summary of the discourse on the treatment of inflammation when it is above or below, that which runs in the operation according to what has been prepared for the form of inflammation is very diverse."
"And the skilled artisan always prepares everything in every possible way that it is possible for him to restore the figure to its natural form or near to it, and this illness according to what suits him of the operation and instruments in the most favorable circumstances."
"Chapter .xv."
"Of adhesion of the eyelid to the conjunctiva or to the cornea."
When this condition occurs in many men, such that the eyelid is solidified above with albumen of egg white, and prohibited from its natural movement and functions, then you should insert the edge of a knife beneath the eyelid and lift it upwards or stretch it open with a hook.
Next, you should incise the adhesion with a fine spatula, which is not too sharp to avoid harming the tissues. Use one that is somewhat blunt so as not to cause discomfort to the patient during the operation, and carefully move the spatula to avoid damaging the eye.
Your incision should extend just enough to release that adhesion, allowing the eyelid to return naturally to its original form and for all the adhesions to be healed.
Next, you should apply saltwater to the eye, using which you will rinse it clean; or, dissolve sugar of lead in water and use this solution instead.
Then, gently separate the eyelid from the eye using cotton soaked in egg white, and apply a compress made of linen infused with egg white. On the third day, begin applying consolidating ointments to promote healing.
Chapter XVI.
Of incision of the nail and caruncle of the lacrimal apparatus.
Know that there are two types of nail: one is nervous and similar to hard skin; the other is non-nervous and similar to congealed white humor. When the latter is touched by forceps, it may become detached and the forceps may not grasp it properly.
"And both species begin only from the larger tear duct, which gradually covers the eye, prohibiting light and its movement."
"Then the manner of operating in the incision is that the patient holds their head back while you open their eyelids, lift the eyelid with your thumb, and carefully grasp the edge of it with tweezers." "And then you take a needle and insert it into the edge of the eyelid, whether it be that of a horse, cow, ox, or similar, and fold the tip of the needle little by little until it is in the middle of the eyelid, and penetrate it with the needle, and pull the eyelid with thread; extend it to the outer edges and remove excess skin from around the pupil." "And then you follow that thread through behind it."
"And then you incise the remnant in the root of the lacrimal duct with a fine spatula or small forceps, and lift the tissue of the natural lacrimal away so that there is no continuous flow of tears through the incision."
"And sometimes the eyelid is extended with only one edge or thread, as we have said, and then it should be carefully excised with a lion's claw spatula, which has this shape:"
"And be sure that with the spatula you do not touch the corneal tunic and that there is a rupture in it, and that the pupil is perforated."
"Then the incision should be washed with a little salt water or clear honey and left open for another day; and then it should be cured with water until it is healed."
"And if the eyelid is not swollen and you cannot insert the needle or it does not stay in place, then often this type of eyelid is cured with medicines, and is healed by stitching it up again in the division."
"And if you want to incise it, then open the wound of the eyelid and take a fine lion's claw spatula with sharp points shaped like this:" "with fineness." "And if sometimes the eyelid becomes hardened and contracted and stuck in its root, then distill from your mouth into the wound clear honey or rose water or salted water, and close the wound the next day."
"And then continue operating on that eyelid until everything that is of it has been removed, except for the contrary aposteme, which should be left in the wound, for when you close it, cure the aposteme at first so that it may heal."
"And then continue your operation on that eyelid until it is healed."
"If the prominence of the lacrimal caruncle is found in the wound causing great harm, then suspend it with a thread. Incise that from there with one cut, but do not complete the incision so as not to incite continuous tearing."
"Then promptly distill into the lachrymal chief rue and make it saturated so that it may be healed."

Chapter XIX.
On the reduction of a fractured nose
"When you treat a fracture of the nose with cautery or irritating medicine according to its narration and it does not heal, then do not try to set it until you have opened up over the inflammation at its maturity and drawn out all the moisture and pus until the bone is exposed."
"And when the bone is exposed and you see corruption or blackness in it, then scrape it with an instrument shaped thus:"
"And it is called the 'sharp head', and should be made of hard steel with a round head thus, having small holes pierced by a file or awl for fine piercing."
"And place it on the corrupted part of the bone and turn it between your fingers while pressing gently until you know that all corruption has been scraped away."
"And do this several times, then restore the place with drying and astringent remedies."
"Therefore if the place is consolidated and good flesh has been produced there, and the skin has separated from the healthy part and remained for forty days without being renewed or inflamed or having any accident happen to it, then you know that it is healed."
"But if not, then do not try to set it but reduce the fracture according to the shape of the nose in this way: first uncover the broken bone with a file or irritating medicine. And when the bone is exposed, then take tweezers shaped thus:"
"The ends of its iron are triangular, and its shaft is thinly tapered towards the end as seen here."
"And then place it on the bone near the lacrimal duct; lengthen your hand a little from the eye and turn your hand with the tweezers until all the bone has entered, and the patient feels pain because of the wind that escapes through there when you move your hand."
"Then restore the place with drying and astringent medicines as I have told you earlier."
"So when the flesh has grown and the place is hardened, then the matter that formerly flowed outwards returns to the nose, which is now easily produced upon the pain."
Chapter XX.
On the reduction of the prominence of the eye
When the swelling has reached its fullness and no apparent harm or reduction occurs, then you should release the patient, and next follow them, and next place cool compresses on the head without scarification and suck with a good suction cup; and next apply a liniment to the swelling made of aloe, acacia, mustard, and sarcocolia, and finally sprinkle the poultice on the swelling with many powders.
The manner of the powders is that you should take cloths of lion's mane mushrooms, each cloth being folded in four layers; and make them from those mushrooms.
And then place those one on top of the other according to the quantity that the swelling has required. And then place on top of those a hard cloth with strong binding, and repeat the suction cups without scarification; and then remove the suction cups and let the swelling rest day and night.
But if during this time the bandage becomes loose, it should be tightened again.
And likewise remove the bandage day and night as we have said.
And if sometimes the swelling has already been reduced, that is good; and if not, then repeat the poultice with powders, binding, and suction cups until it is healed.
Chapter XXI
Of the incision of the prominence of the tunic of the uvea.
When there is disruption in the tunic of the uvea and it becomes prominent and projects outside the eyelids like a grain of mustard seed, and the shape of a human face appears due to this, and you wish to incise that, then the operation in that case is as follows: You should insert the needle into the depression of the uvea from below upwards, and next insert another needle on the side where the lacrimal gland is located, and make that penetrate and leave the first needle according to its position; and next incise the location of the doubled thread and lift up with that the part of the uvea in the circuit of the needle, and pull it tight.
And next remove the needle and place on top a pad infused in egg white albumen and leave it there until the thread with the uvea falls.
And then dress the wound with something that will comfort it until the inflammation is healed.
And sometimes it happens that the entire part is attached with a band of cloth around the wound where there is a prominent swelling, and then it should be perforated with a fine spatula that comes to the front of the wound, and the humid albume runs down, and thus the wound descends and enters quickly.
And then pull it tight until it is healed.
Chapter XXII
Of the treatment of an inflamed eye.
This illness called aconati is naught but phlegm, which collects in the body like descending water.
To treat this illness, make the patient sit on an upright chair and hold their head firmly in your hands on both sides. Then press the area where you see the phlegm gathering until it stops flowing downwards, and keep their mouth closed so that no air escapes while you do this.
And if it does not flow downwards, know that it is water.
"If the descent is not prepared for the patient as mentioned earlier, then hold the patient's hands and carefully take a thin spatula and insert it over the fatty tissue around the corner of the conjunctiva with the tunica cornea at the entrance (into the wound), until the sanies is expelled."
"Then, once it has been expelled, immediately apply lukewarm water in which honey or gruel made from fenugreek and honey has been dissolved."
"And likewise, treat other causes until the patient is healed."
"Chapter XXII."
"On the treatment of watery discharge from the eye."
"We have already discussed the types of watery discharge and which ones are suitable to be treated with speech therapy, according to the patient's condition."
"Then, make the patient sneeze into a handkerchief and have them wipe their eyes with it, using firm pressure."
Approach and place your left hand near the eyelid of the patient's left eye if the eye with water is the left one; otherwise, use your right hand if the eye is on the right side.
Approach and with your right hand take a towel if the eye is left; otherwise, use your left hand if the eye is right.
Approach the tip of the towel near the corner of the eye along the thickness of the eyelid near the inner tear duct, and carefully wipe the eye with the towel using your hand.
Enter the eyelid and wait until you feel that the towel has reached its wet spot.
Make sure the path of the towel is parallel to the measurement from the pupil's edge to the end of the pupil's darkness, which is the corner of the eye; thus you will see the pupil with clarity through the cornea.

Then wait a moment; if the water has flowed downwards, then gently wipe once more to ensure that no towel lint remains.
Then, when it is dry and no longer flows downwards, gently remove the towel with ease, turn your hand slowly bit by bit, dissolve a little of gem-quality salt in water, wash the inside of the eye with that, and then apply cotton wool soaked in rose oil and alum water to the outer corner of the eye, and tie it there.
Let us pause here on this subject, as those who are of our time should wait upon that which is written in books about this matter.

Chapter XXIV.
Concerning the treatment of flesh torn from the nose.
When different pieces of flesh are born in the nose that are attached to each other, and one cause of this is the assembly of many heavy scorpions or large polyps, this illness is called "polypus" because it resembles that type of polyp. And its flesh is cancerous and black in color; but it is not that kind of flesh called "lion's flesh" which is not black in color.
Therefore, in that case where it is not fraudulent or cancerous lion's flesh, you should make the patient sneeze between your hands and hold them over the sun, then blow his nose and pinch him on those pieces of flesh. Then remove that [polyp] from its exterior parts, and then carefully cut off with a sharp pointed spatula what you have grasped of those pieces on one side until you know that all the flesh has been removed. But if any cause remains for which excision is possible, then quickly remove it with one of the subtle instruments with ease so that no cause remains. But if it is bleeding profusely or an abscess appears, then pause and do what is necessary. Or if it is one of the malignant abscesses, then cut it out and cauterize that [area] until there is no more bleeding and all the cavities are open.
Then let him be sprinkled in the nose with a mixture of vinegar and water or vinegar alone. But if the nose is open and its moisture extends to the palate, then know that it has already been healed.
But if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, then know that there is flesh torn from the upper bones of the nose that has not been removed by excision.
Therefore, you should insert a feather into his nostril with some thickness, and rub it in both nostrils, pausing between each rubbing for the length of one finger or more. Then generate the sneeze and insert an extremity of the feather into the nose with the reed or with another cause that is possible for him.
And after that has been done, let him throw his breath into the nostrils until it reaches the canals of the nose, and let it be exhaled over his throat, because many children at school often do this action, and it is an easy thing to do for anyone who wishes.
Then pause the two extremities of the feather, one extremity that exits over the nose and the other that remains in the nose. Then administer a suture of flesh with the threads on the feather, and do this until you know that the flesh is attached to the threads of the feather.
Then remove the feather and pause in the nose with the abstraction of blood for one day, and do this for three days or more until the ointment has rotted all that is left of the flesh.
Then at the end of the cause, pause in the nose with a lead cannula for several days until it is healed.
But if you desire an operation that dries up, use cautery with it.

"Chapter 25"
"About nostrils that are in the outer parts of the nose."
"It is rarely seen that a nostril appears on the outer part of the nose, and it is much admired and praised in those days when one sees such."
"And for this reason, you should cut off that nostril at the beginning of its appearance, and remove all of it." "And then pause upon the place where you have cut, cauterize or apply a burning medicine there."
"But if its excision is delayed until it becomes much admired, then consider whether it is walled-off, hard, of dark color and has little sensation. If so, do not touch that area with iron for it is a cranky ulcer; many times that which you incise may spread great mischief over the person who had it."
"And if the ulcer is of mild appearance and not dark-colored, sometimes incision may be possible throughout it. Therefore evacuate the disease and incise it without fear, then cure the area with something that dries and constricts until it heals."
"Chapter 26"
"About the suture of the nose, lips and ear when continuity is disrupted by plague or scarring."
"You should know that when disruption of continuity occurs in one of these cartilages (nose, lips or ear), little is gained from that operation except for a few men."
"Therefore, when some cause occurs to those parts (nose, lips or ear), you should consider if it is a fresh plague with its own blood. Then join the two lips of the plague with suture, and afterward cure it until it heals."
"And if the lips of disrupted continuity are already separated, and each is fairly healthy, then you should cut out each section of its apparent path until no blood appears." "And then join the two lips with suture and strengthen them. On top of that, sprinkle dragon's blood powder and heat it three times, then place a piece of diaphoretic plaster or some other consolidating plaster on the wound for two to three days, after which remove it and replace the plaster until it adheres by itself. Then cure with an ointment until healed."
"But the manner of suture is that you approximate the disrupted continuity either with needles as we have recommended for abdominal wounds or use fine thread as you know how."
"Chapter 27"
"For the extraction of those causes that appear in both lips in cases of internal disease."
"Often seen among many men in cases of internal disease are hard tumors resembling gristle on both sides of the lips; some small and others larger."
"Therefore you should turn the lips and split each of those hardnesses on both sides, and after the incision make the wound bleed completely until it stops flowing; then wash the area with vinegar and treat it with an astringent water to heal."
"Chapter XXVIII."
"The Incision of Adherent Flesh in the Gums."
"Often seen is this: over the adherent flesh of the gum which the ancients called albulus. Therefore you should suspend it with a thread or hold it with forceps and incise it down to its root, allowing the wound to drain."
"And then apply a poultice made of healing herbs or sprinkle powder that is astringent or caustic over the wound."
"If that flesh returns, then incise it secondarily, and cauterize it, for it will not return otherwise."

"And therefore you must do this: place the patient between your thighs and press their head against the back of their neck, and scrape off the scales from those teeth where such appearances occur, causing it to resemble sand, so that no cause remains. And this is done regarding blackness, greenness-yellowishness, and other discolorations."
"So if the above is not what you desire at the beginning of this section, then you may repeat the procedure on another day, or on the second and third days until you reach your desired outcome."

"Chapter XXX."
"Tooth Extraction."
"The tooth that you are treating for its pain may grow again and require complete removal because there is no reason why it should not regrow once it has been removed since it is a substance prone to recurrence in its removal."
"Therefore when the patient is forced to have that tooth removed, you must be firmly certain what the painful tooth is because often the pain occurs in a healthy tooth and if you remove the wrong one, the pain will not stop until the actual painful tooth is removed, as we have seen happen during operations by barbers."
"Therefore when you are certain what the painful tooth is and know it well, then you should scarify around the tooth with spathum in which there is some virtue until it dissolves from the tooth's gum completely. Afterwards remove that with your tweezers, or with delicate forceps little by little until it comes loose."
"Then use your large forceps with good traction or sturdy construction, and grasp the head of the disease firmly between them so that it does not slip away from you. Then remove the tooth straightly in such a way that neither breaks nor causes greater pain to the patient."
"And therefore if it is not forgotten, then take one of those instruments and insert it on either side of the tooth with ease and effort for its removal as was done at the beginning."
"But if the tooth is broken or decayed, then you must first cover that break with wax and strengthen it with the extremity of a thin wire so that it may not be further broken during your constriction upon it with forceps."
"And you must work carefully with the scarification around all parts of the gum and guard your strength so that you do not break or tear it apart and return upon the patient for a greater pain than the first one."
"And beware of doing what many ignorant barbers do in their foolishness and boldness regarding extraction without administering what we have recommended. For often they cause great illnesses upon men which are more difficult to treat than the tooth itself, leaving behind roots entirely or partially removed, or removing teeth with some bones from the jaw as we have often witnessed."
"And after the extraction of the tooth, wash out the mouth with hot water mixed with salt."
"And if there is blood flowing from it afterwards, as often happens, then take some quantity of sage and sprinkle it upon the wound. And if this does not suffice, cauterize."
"The form of the forceps and thin tweezers with which the tooth is grasped at the beginning should be long in extremity, short in handle, and thick so that they may not bend when using them."
"And let their handles be like those of tongs inside so that when you squeeze with them they do not bend, and their extremities are short."
"And let them be made of India iron well-tempered and made with straight extremities. And on the extremities of these have teeth which fit into each other and grasp tightly for constriction. Sometimes the extremities of these are shaped like the beak of a bird called the ciconia, which is hooked, and they are of strong constriction."
