"Chapter XXXII."
"Regarding the treatment of prominent teeth compared to others."
If teeth protrude beyond their natural course due to that form being disturbed, especially in women and even more so in venerable elders; therefore you must consider: if one tooth is not close to another tooth, and no surgery or splint can help, then that one should be removed; but if it is attached to another tooth, then you should cut that one with this instrument whose shape is like a pig's bristle, made of Indian iron with an extremely sharp point.
And your incision should be deep enough so that you can remove that tooth in three days due to the hardness of the tooth, without damaging any other teeth.
And if it is an erupted tooth that needs grinding, then grind it with an Indian iron file whose shape is like this:
And let it all be of Indian iron and sharp; and have many small pointed teeth like those on a file with which the tooth is gently filed little by little over many days, so that no other tooth is damaged or broken. And afterwards clean it well with thread and scrape it with sharp razors.
And if it is a tooth where one part is chipped and irritates the tongue, then you should grind that edge until its roughness is smoothed out and flattened so that the tongue does not rub against it and speech is not impeded.
Chapter XXXIII
Of the restoration of damaged teeth with gold or silver foil.
When teeth are damaged due to concussion and removal by percussion or fracture, and the patient cannot eat because of it, and you have treated them with astringent medications, but your treatment has not been effective, then for those that are strong enough, they should be restored with gold foil and not silver, because silver quickly tarnishes and turns black, while gold never changes.
And the foil should be in such fineness and thinness according to the quantity that can fit between the teeth; and the method of application is as follows: take the foil and fold it in half between two healthy teeth, and then shape it with two curves of the foil between the damaged ones, or one curve if there is only one, so that the foil reaches the healthy part of the other tooth. And then gradually fill in the space where you started, using your hand gently and skillfully so as not to damage the tooth.
And use a tool with which you press the foil between the roots of the teeth so that it does not shift.
And then cut off the excess ends of the foil with forceps or scissors, and adapt them in each place with gestures, and turn them over and hide them between the healthy tooth and the damaged one, so that they do not cause injury to the tongue. And then press it down as tightly as possible.
But if it comes loose or breaks off, reinforce it with more foil in the same manner at all times.
And this is how you repair two healthy teeth and two damaged ones, as shown in the illustration below:
And when one or two teeth return to their original position after the fracture, they should be repaired as described above, and then replaced.
This is not something that just anyone can do; it requires skill and expertise.
Sometimes it is convenient to use the bones of a cow as a substitute for teeth. These should be shaped like teeth and placed in the location where the tooth is missing, and then strengthened with foil as described above, and they will serve well for a long time.
Chapter XXXIV
Of the incision of the frenulum that extends onto the tongue and interferes with speech.
This frenum that hangs down from the tongue sometimes occurs naturally or is acquired accidentally due to a healed injury.
The procedure is as follows: have the patient open their mouth and hold their head still. Then elevate the tongue and cut through the frenum with a scalpel along its width until the tongue is freed from its attachment.
But if there is some hardness or thickness in the frenum due to scar tissue from a healed injury, then you should first grease it with oil and cut through it along its width until you have completely severed the frenum and dissolved the scar tissue.
Be careful not to make a deep incision in the flesh of the front part of the tongue, lest you cut too deeply and cause bleeding.
Then rinse the incision site with warm water or vinegar or salty water, and then apply a bandage to the tongue. Then tell the patient to keep their tongue out of their mouth at all times for several days to prevent reattachment of the frenum.
But if bleeding occurs, apply a compress soaked in vinegar. If the bleeding continues, then cauterize the area with a silver nitrate cautery stick, which is appropriate for this purpose. And then treat it according to other causes until it heals.
Chapter XXXV
"For the extraction of a ranula from under the tongue."
Occasionally, an aposteme resembling a small blister may appear under the tongue and prevent its normal functioning.
And the operation in this case is to have the patient open their mouth wide before you, and examine the aposteme.
And if it appears dark or black in colour, hard, where the patient feels no sensation, then do not touch that part as it is cancerous.
And if it appears white with humidity, then insert the tweezers into it and incise that little mucous membrane, and cut it completely; and if blood begins to flow during your operation, then pause for a moment, so that it may cease flowing.
And then return to your work until you have completely removed it, ensuring that it is washed with vinegar and salt. Then treat it with the other cure until it has healed.
Chapter XXXVI
Concerning the extraction of an aposteme from both ears, and that which is situated in the throat, as well as other apostemes.
When a swelling appears in the throat, it is called glandular, which are often joined together and located externally, known as the ears. If you treat them with water according to what has been said in this division and they do not heal, then consider whether the aposteme is hard, dark coloured, and insensitive. If so, do not touch it with iron.
And if it appears red in colour and the root is thick, then do not touch it with iron due to the flow of blood. Let it ripen on its own, and then you may remove it or it will burst by itself.
"When it has a white color, consistency, and its root is delicate, then that one should be incised."
"And before your operation, consider whether the abscess has already been opened by cautery and is fully drained or if it has decreased with some decrease. Then seat the patient facing the sun, place their head on a high pillow, open their mouth, and have the servant press their tongue down with a noble instrument, shaped as follows:"

Then take pincers and place them on it, and pull it outwards as much as possible." "And after this, if you manage to remove some of the coats, then promptly incise it with that instrument, shaped as follows:"
"And after this, if you manage to remove some of the coats, then promptly incise it with that instrument, shaped as follows:" "And it resembles forceps, but its ends are curved so that the points of each are directed towards the other. It should be made of hardened steel."
"But if this instrument is not available to you, then incise it with a scalpel, shaped as follows: sharp on one side and blunt on the other."
"And having made one incision, make another according to this same method of cutting. Then wash the wound clean with fresh water."
"But if there is bleeding, wash it with water from a decoction of rosehip or myrtle leaves, similar to those remedies that have the power to stop bleeding. And continue treating it until it is healed."
"And sometimes, other abscesses appear on the glands or around those two ears. Incise them in the same manner as I have described for incising two abscesses at once."
"And I was called to treat a woman who had an abscess that had grown in her gland. It was dark-colored and painless, and it had already closed the mouth of the gland. The woman was breathing with difficulty, and she had been prohibited from eating or drinking water. She was close to death if something hadn't happened within one or two days."
"And the abscess had grown so much that it had formed two openings through which pus issued from two ducts."
"Therefore I extracted it vaginally and remained in one of their orifices, and removed that [organ], and a large portion was torn away. Then I inserted my finger into where the other passage begins, then I pressed the mouth closed and held its tongue down. And then I placed the orifice in that abscess."
"And you cut off a large part of it, but there was only a little blood flowing from it." "Therefore it was the death of that woman, and she immediately began drinking water, and ate food. And I kept incising that abscess many times over a long period of time, but another abscess formed in its place, which continued to grow longer."
"Therefore I applied heat and cauterized the wound of it, then added more [material]. And then I wandered around and did not know what God had done to that woman because of me."
Chapter XXXVII
**On Incising a Swelling When It Is Abscessed**
When catarr descends to the lung and is thickened and lengthened, then it is called perpendicular; but if it is at its beginning, thick and rounded, then it is called phlegm.
But if the cure is not achieved with what has been said in this section, and especially when an abscess has already formed but is still hidden and subtle, then you should incise where it becomes rounded; and if it has reached that length and is sanguineous, of dark color or black, and does not cause pain, then you should fear the incision, for there is danger to the patient in this case.
And when you find it according to the manner that I have indicated by its whiteness and length, then you should cause the illness to cease and press the tongue of it with an instrument whose shape is appropriate for this purpose, and then place a new bandage on top of it, draw it downwards and incise it with one of two instruments which are used in the incision of abscesses.
And you should not incise more than what is appropriate to the natural term without addition, for if you incise too much, you will wound it.
And in the incision, use what has been recommended in the incision of abscesses, and heal it afterwards until it is healed.
But if the illness is frightened by the incision of it, then you should use a cautery in its cauterization without fear, and the manner of cautery in it is not other than with hot water, and that is to place the head of the illness on the little finger, and press the tongue of it with the instrument which has been mentioned, and take some of the water which has been mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and apply it with a live coal, and do so neither too thick nor too subtle, and fill with that the concavity of the instrument whose shape is this:
Let the extremity of the concavity in which the medicine has been placed be thus shaped as the concavity of a spoon of ray, and place the instrument with the medicine on the wound, and let the illness drip onto its side so that no saliva or spittle from the mouth of him who receives the internal medicine falls into his throat lest he choke.
And then you place your hand with the medicine on the uvula and express it for about half an hour until you see that it has become blackened and settled by the biting of the medicine.
And if you wish, take cotton and envelop that on the extremity of the ray, and submerge the cotton in the medicine, and insert the ray with the cotton into a cannula from above until the cotton adheres to that cannula, and do this many times until you succeed in what you want from the cautery of the wound, and then leave it alone because it will dry out and fall off after about three or four days.
And if you need to repeat the medicine, repeat it, and then afterwards cleanse the cautery around the wound with cotton dipped in border, and remove with that what is on the circuit of the wound from the medicine, and wash it with hot water, and dress it afterwards with embrocation, and finally with compresses until it has healed.
And this type of treatment was saved that incision and cautery were both long from fear.
Sometimes the uvula is cured with something so subtle that cautery and incision are not needed, because it is treated with sublimation in this manner: take calamint, hyssop, oregano, rue, saffron, camomile, broadleaf plantain, and other similar herbs of the plants, adjust all those causes, or some of them, in an earthenware pot, and let them be immersed with sour wine, and boil; and let the earthenware pot be well covered with dough, and let there be in the middle of the pot a tube over which is placed a concave instrument made of silver or brass.
And let the extremity be inserted into the mouth of the patient until the vapor can reach the uvula above the uvula until the uvula becomes quite obscured.
And then repeat this many times until it has dried out, and make sure that you do not perform this treatment at the beginning of the formation of an aposteme, because it would too much stimulate the aposteme, and you should not do that, but rather await the declaration of the aposteme from the cautery.
But if you do not have this instrument present, then take a cane and attach at its extremity a clod of earth, so that the mouth of the patient is covered, because the clod of earth prevents the vapor from burning the mouth.
And this treatment is good for health.
Chapter XXXVI
Of the extraction of spines and of what adheres in the throat and other causes.
Many times adhesions are found in the peritoneum or spine of the feet or some other cause.
Therefore you must remove that which is visible of those [adhesions], upon which the eye catches sight, because as you press the tongue with an instrument beforehand, it will be declared to you what is in the throat.
And that which is not apparent and is hidden in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach, because easily the cause attached to the throat will be forgotten through vomiting; or else have the patient swallow a piece of napkin or a bit of lettuce leaf or a mouthful of dry bread; or take a piece of damp sea-sponges and tie it tightly with flax, and make the patient swallow that, because when it arrives at the place where its spines are extracted, they will be removed then. And also take an eel and tie it tightly with flax, and let it be within the table and softly be extracted; or else take a porridge and softly place it and softly bring it out.
But if those causes which we have mentioned are not forgotten from those [adhesions], then you must use an instrument of lead made in this way:
"It should be larger than a small one, and at its tip there is a concavity which you will insert into its mouth with ease."
"And the patient raises their head upwards, and be careful that the contact of their forehead with the throat causes them no discomfort or pain."
"However, the patient should preferably insert it themselves, using their knowledge of the location of the cause annexed and placing it downwards, then pulling their hand up with the instrument, all according to the quantity that has been prepared so as not to forget."

"On the extraction of a blood clot annexed to the throat."

"Chapter XL"
"This chapter deals with the treatment of boils and their incision."
"Abscesses are various types, having many forms, according to their memory recalled in this book."
"And they differ in perforation and section of their form by two methods: one is for the species of abscesses within themselves; and what we learn about humidity."
"And the second method is near the places where accidents happen to the body, because an abscess that occurs in the head differs from one that occurs in the buttocks; and an abscess in the fleshy place differs from one that occurs at the joint; and each of them has its own treatment through surgery."
"And more about abscesses, some of which should not be perforated but rather await their natural ripening or completion."
"And there are other abscesses that must be opened when they are hard and not ripe according to their completion, such as those that are near the joints. For an abscess when it is near a joint, its essence extends into what is in its circuit, and often its ligaments or nerves of that joint become corrupted, which causes contraction of that member; or it is near a main member, and if you delay its opening until it is ripe, it can harm the main member; or it is near the buttocks, therefore open one that is not fully matured. And do not perforate it in crude condition with incomplete digestion, but rather that which is near the buttocks, so that it does not corrupt the anus and extend into the inner parts of the buttocks, and cause a fistula to be formed, or else let it heal without being opened." "And so you should know the time for opening an abscess, and that is when it has ripened."
"And you should know that an abscess is ripe when there is cessation of pain and fever, and around the decrease in redness and swelling, and the sharp point of the abscess, and other signs."
"And because you should know that the opening should be made where there is purulent matter, away from the abscess itself, and coming from the summit of its swelling."
"And always make the opening along the length of the flesh or body, if the abscesses are in the regions of the thigh or calf, and in locations of the sinews, nerves, arteries; and finally, in all locations where it is suitable; for those that are reflected, use reflection in opening them."
"But when the abscess is in a fleshy location, it is better to leave its opening until digestion has fully confirmed its completion, as we have said; for if you open it before that time, the wound of the abscess will lengthen and become very dirty, and often its lips are hardened and the depth of it increases."
"But some abscesses must be opened across the width of the flesh or body due to necessity, or according to what that member requires."
"And you should make a small opening for large abscesses and wide or multiple incisions according to the diversity of the size of the abscesses."
"And there are other abscesses in which it is necessary to make an incision with a curved blade and cut it when it has been made, as soon as it has reached its completion, such as those that happen in cases of dropsy and buboes."
"And there are those that are incised with three angles of sectioning; and there are those in which it is cut like the figure of a miter leaf, such as the abscesses of the anus."
"And there are some in which round sectioning and crescent-shaped sectioning are used, similar to those."
"But for those abscesses that do not present themselves as deeply seated abscesses, you should open them with a superficial or flat opening only."
"And when the abscess is large and has collected much pus, you should open it but do not try to remove all the pus at once; take out a portion of it, then pack the abscess again the next day, gradually removing larger portions each time until it is completely emptied."
"And especially if the patient is a young child, woman in labor, infant, or elderly person in a state of decay; for many times the vital spirit is resolved along with the exit of the pus, and often the patient dies while being operated on."
"So be very careful with this chapter, and especially when opening these abscesses, you should clean the wounds and consider whether the wound of the abscess is small or a flat section; then administer the proper dressings or old rags. And if the abscess is large and the incisions are wide, then you should pack each wound separately until they heal together."
"And if a portion of the blade or curvature is cut off in the abscess, you should fill it with old lint or thread made from linen cloth, just as when dressing wounds without moisture. Then tighten it on the third day and proceed to treat it with what is appropriate for wounds until it heals."
"But if blood flows during your operation, then administer water boiled with vinegar in which a linen cloth has been soaked, and place it on the location of the bleeding many times."
"But if the bleeding persists, then you should administer remedies and treatment, using the powders that I have recommended in many places throughout this book and its divisions."
"But if it is wintertime and the location of the abscess has many nerves, then you should sprinkle powders made from hot wine and oil on that location."
"And if it is summertime and the locations are fleshy, then you should apply powders moistened with water and oil or wine and oil, all of which has been heated until the third day, as we have said. Then drain the abscess, clean it, and administer whatever is appropriate for its treatment until it heals."
"And this is what is necessary for the knowledge of treating abscesses in general; but according to the method of distinction, I have already mentioned how each type of abscess should be treated individually."
Chapter XLII.
Chapter XLII: Incision of Abscesses that Occur on the Neck
In the neck, small abscesses occur, and they are of a type that contains tunics that are made from them; and there are many species of them.
And among them are pimples, and some contain moisture like lime. And among them are those that contain moisture resembling dust, similar to them; and some are stony and hard.
In the incision of all of them, and in their extraction, there is nothing to fear, for you should know that their extraction does not cause great injury.
The operation for incising them is that you express them with an instrument called the trephine, whose form is shown below, until you know that it contains.
For if what it contains is moisture, then cut it open with a longitudinal incision using a superficial incision according to this form:
And begin the incision along line BG until line FG. Then, once the moisture has been evacuated, strip away that which contains this moisture, leaving nothing behind, for it often returns if some cause remains.
Then immerse the wound in Egyptian ointment, if available, or else in water and salt. Fill it with this and leave it for another day, for with this you will corrode all that remains of its film.
"Then repeat this operation on that area with Egyptian ointment secondly and thirdly if necessary, ensuring there is no remaining cause of that inflammation; then treat the wound until it is healed."
"If an abscess contains fat knots, then you should cut into it following this shape:" "The section should have the shape of a cross, and cut incisions between its two lips and tear it apart entirely, exerting your strength to extract the tunic that contains it."
"But if your attempt fails, then do what I told you first."
"And similarly perform the operation and treatment on an incised abscess according to what I have told you; incision over an incised abscess is easier because it contains little blood and humidity."
"And sometimes there are cases of these abscesses that occur on the head in some people who have little humidity; this is why you should not cut into an abscess on the head of an elderly woman and tear it apart like a deaf, rough, white stone which cannot be broken down, otherwise she would be harmed by it."
"But in other accidental abscesses on the head that are not mentioned here, such as those that appear on children's heads or behind the ears, their incision should be a superficial one."
"And leave the perforation of those whose bottom is lower so that the body may be relieved from low-lying inflammation."
"And then treat those with what is suitable for their treatment."
"Chapter XLII"
Scrofula section: Those that occur in the neck.
Many times these tumors appear on the neck, armpits and groin; sometimes they occur in other parts of the body.

"And then take a reed and place it on the prominent location of the caecum, and press it against the front of the belly."
"And then cut the two prominent locations on the extremity of the reed over the caecum, and adjust them with a suture one to the other."
"And then remove the extremity of the reed, and do not insert it into the caecum completely, nor extend the wound, nor other causes such as those which you should know about in the treatment of intestinal hernia."
"And then treat it with the treatment of ulcers, and when you incise the membranes, clean them and restore the ulcer so that it is consolidated; for the caecum contracts and the prominence of rupture is not adjusted."
"And cautery is better in this location because it is closer to health."
Chapter LXVIII
Concerning the softening of the backbone of the testicles.
Very often, the backbone of the testicles in some men is softened because the flesh that is between them is also softened, and this condition deserves attention.
Therefore, it is necessary for someone who wants to treat this condition to make the patient lie on his back and cut all the softened backbone that is over the natural backbone, and then adjust two lips with a suture.
And if you wish, cut at the beginning of the softened backbone's excess with three or four cuts and close it with firm sutures.
And then incise between the sutures, and treat it with the treatment of other ulcers until it heals and the membranes fall off.
De la cusida de la codena dels testiculs.
Castration
Know that castration is forbidden by our law, but for some reason I remember it in this book; and it is not necessary to remember it except for two manners: the first is so that it may be known in the science of medicine when one asks about its treatment; and the second manner is because we often have need of castration in other beasts for our benefit, such as with mules, oxen, pigs, and similar animals.
And thus it is said that castration is done in two ways: either by incision or by cutting open.
But in that which is done by incision, the method of operation is that we make the beast lie down in cold water until its testicles become softened and relaxed, and then they may be cut off. And therefore take those [testicles] with your hand before they are resolved or appear outside the touch of the skin.
But in castration done by cutting open and removing, you should hold the beast and press on the cord of its testicles with your left hand.
And then cut the suspension ligament, and make an incision above each testicle with one stroke so that both emerge at once.
And then cut those [testicles] off as soon as they have emerged. And do not leave anything on the scrotum except for a small piece of skin over the veins.
And this method of castration by incision is better than that done by cutting open and removing because it leaves some cause of the testicles so that the beast desires copulation.
And then dress the wound until it heals.
Chapter LXX.
Of the treatment of hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in men occurs in two ways. The first is when something appears like a female vulva between the testicles in place of the space that should be there.
Sometimes urine flows from that place where the testicles are connected.
But in women there is only one kind: it is when the vulva appears on the pubis like two testicles of a man, with a little opening towards the posterior, just as the male penis has and two testicles.
And there are three types of treatment for this condition: two for men and one for women. And it is necessary to cut those joined flesh parts until the flow of that emission stops, and then dress them with the treatment for other wounds.
And in the second kind in men where urine flows from that place where the testicles are connected, there is neither treatment nor operation to be done there.

Chapter LXXII.
Of the remedy for alopecia.
It is advisable that the womb of the woman is not pierced or drawn out. And whether it is a natural or an accident.
An accident is when the illness has preceded it, and that is done either by flesh not properly adjusted, or by a thin or thick skin.
And it is done either in the front of the mother's belly, or on her sides, or above or below the navel, and it inhibits conception, pregnancy, and childbirth; and it particularly inhibits menstruation.
And the knowledge of that is made through examination of the mother's womb, if the dilation is apparent; but if it is not apparent, then you will search for it with your fingers or with a speculum.
But if the dilation is due to thin skin and it is apparent at both lips of the vulva, then you will cut and tear that.
And if there is pressure on both labia majora, then you should apply pressure with your fingers at the thickest part of each one.
And when the woman is on her back with her legs spread wide, then you will spread both labia majora with force until that thin skin is broken and the dilation is opened.
Then take some linen and oil and place it on the location, and press gently with your hand for a little while so that the incision does not close up.
But if the skin is thick and hard, then you must incise it with a broad knife or with a myrtle leaf.
But if the dilation is due to inflammation, then suspend that with an ointment and incise it.

"And then insert a wide lead cannula so that the wound is not lightly sealed."
"Keep it on for a few days and apply boiled water to cleanse it."
"And then treat it with another consolidation cure until it is healed."
"Sometimes, especially in the case of other flesh wounds, this method should be followed." "But if it is a hard boil, make sure that there is no contradiction with iron in any way."
Chapter LXXIII.
Of the treatment of hemorrhoids and prolapse of the rectum that occurs in women's genitals.
Hemorrhoids are a condition of many veins around the anus, from which much blood flows continuously. And when old hemorrhoids form clots, they become hard.
"And as I have already said in the division of species and symptoms of these, I will say here which ones receive treatment and which do not."
Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids and hard clots when they are at the entrance of the anus and cannot be felt, in those cases there is no treatment with iron.
But those that are at the opening of the anus and can be felt, those are the ones that can be treated.
And you must make the woman lie on her back and extend her buttocks with both hands or a rough cloth, and then incise them with scissors.
And then sprinkle on it the flows of blood from one of the incised powders without biting it, such as cassia and similar drugs.
Then make her fast for an hour, and then apply a hot compress to that area.
And if the bleeding persists, then make her take a decoction of sumac and oak bark and cranberry seeds and walnut shells and similar drugs.
And then take some barley flour and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with that mixture to apply on the back of her.
And if the blood is cut off, it's good. But if not, then adhere with two leeches and scarify the breasts without bloodletting.
And then take some wool and soak it in juice of cilantro or in juice of sage or in juice of agrimony with red wine, and apply it to the location; and then dress the location with a poultice until it is healed.
And dress it until it is healed.
Chapter LXXIV
Of the perforation of a haemorrhoid accidentally in the anus.
Many species of apostumes happen accidentally in the anus, such as cancer and stone apostume and ulcerous and adherent and creeping and fistulous hemorrhoids and raw ones and hard clots and others. And I have already spoken of these illnesses and their species and their symptoms, and the treatments for them in the division.
And it is necessary that I say in this treatise about the cauterization of a cauter that appears in the anus when it comes from those apostumes that are curable, and if you want to know how the operation of it is done with iron.
Then you must consider if the pain of the aposteme at its beginning is sharp with percussion and swelling and fever, and if it becomes reddened and if you can feel it, then do not cut it open with a perforation, but dress it with what helps with ripening until the sharpness of the symptoms ceases.
And then you must make the woman lie down on two pillows; and she should recline on her back and adjust her feet towards the side of the bed below the belly, and spread out her thighs, and pause her arms away from her breasts, and tie each thigh with a cloth in an appropriate manner.
And then the midwife should stand on the right side and administer the instrument with which the incision of the anus is made, whose shape will come in those cases that are mentioned below.
And it is necessary that when you want to administer this instrument, you should stand at the back of the woman's buttocks, and that only as much of the instrument enters into the anus as the width of the anus, so that it does not enter too deep and harm the illness. But if the instrument is larger than the width of the anus, then you must pause powders on the texture of the anus so that it hinders the entrance of any instrument into the anus.
And it is necessary that you pause the lever that runs in the instrument on the right side and above, so that the one who administers the instrument holds it and turns the lever until the incision of the anus is opened.
And when the excision appears and is touched with the hand and it is loose and moist, then you must dry it quickly with the head of a spoon.
And when the sickness is evacuated, then you must pause in the wound a wick soaked in rose oil or verdigris oil, which has some astringency, and pause the cloth on the section in the width of the anus.
And then cover the anus with clean wool immersed in water in which mallows have been boiled.
And then it should be dressed properly for two days with a poultice suitable for that purpose until it is healed.
And sometimes the anus and the wound are washed in this way: they are washed with water and honey, and sometimes with water in which rose leaves or long-stalked comfrey have been boiled, and then it returns to the poultice.
And if the wound is deep in the anus and swollen, then it is necessary that you abstain from the cure of it with iron, but dress it with what we have said in the division.
Chapter LXXV.
To teach midwives how to treat the breech births when they come out in an unnatural position.
It is necessary that the midwife knows at the beginning the figure of a natural childbirth by its signs, and it is that when you see the woman pressing down below and desiring to smell the air, and then she is relieved by what comes out above her, and rushes quickly to expel the child, then you know that this birth is according to nature, and it is the expulsion of it with its head coming out first, and the second one hanging or suspended from the navel.
Therefore, when you see those signs, then it is necessary that the belly of it be pressed so that the child comes out lightly when its head comes out first and thus the second one comes out clean from all impurities with good cleansing.
But that which is otherwise than this birth is unnatural and blameworthy, for when the child comes out with its feet first and its body comes out before its head and its feet, and one of its hands or even one of its legs or its belly comes out first, and thus it turns with its back upwards, such figures are blameworthy.
Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skilled in all these matters and to guard against error and deception.
And here I show you all figures of those and what kind they are by which it may be understood through this and be placed on this.
When heat is exhaled upon the head due to natural greediness, and it is strong in women and difficult to bear, especially when their virtue has already weakened, then they become feverish. This occurs because women hold on to resentment, and they evaporate the congestion from their chest with fenugreek cooked with oil.
Then insert the syringe between her thighs and fill it with that second liquid or else dig with your nail into that which is inside her and remove whatever humidity there is. And press on the woman's belly until the fetus emerges.
But if it does not come out, then it is necessary that the woman be smeared with dough made from chickpeas and dough made from fenugreek with cumin.
And then command it to be smeared on her and have her sneeze with conditions; and cover her mouth and nose with something for an hour, because the fetus will soon be forgotten.
And if both hips of the fetus are forgotten at the beginning, then you must reduce them little by little with ease. And if the hips are not turned correctly and the fetus dies, then cut them open and remove the remnants of the fetus or else tie its body with cloth and remove it gently, because it will soon be forgotten.

"Treatment of fistulas that are formed there:"
"The fistulas that are formed in the lower part of the buttocks are usually large and thick, which are formed near the anus outside or in the space between one buttock."
"And it is one fistula or many."
"And with this thickness being old and running with moist, thick white humors or thin pus, and sometimes there are penetrating passages in these fistulas."
"And these passages are known by what comes out of them through discharge and through windiness; and sometimes the disease is from discharge, and it often comes out of those worms."
"And sometimes there are penetrating passages from these fistulas into the bladder and into the meatus of the penis; and some of those passages are into the junction of the vulva and into the notch of the scrotum."
"And what is known as a penetrating fistula that enters the anus and is not penetrating is this: you put your finger inside the anus, and then insert a thin probe made of brass or iron into the fistula where there is no turning."
"But if there is a turn in that place, then insert into it a thin probe made of lead or horsehair until you feel the probe or hair on your finger."
"And if you do not feel it at all and there is no cause of discharge or worms or windiness coming from the anus, as we have said, then know that it is not penetrating, and then proceed to treatment."
"And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the meatus of the penis, then its meaning is the emission of urine from there and prohibition of it until that place has healed in medicine."
"But if it is penetrating into the junction of the vulva or into the bone and causes pain in the area, then its sign is that the probe enters there if there is no turning inside the bone, and there is pain in the area of the joint; and that pus always comes out from there; and that medicine and ointment are ineffective, nor does it heal."
"And in all those penetrating fistulas, there is no complete cure, and the cure of those is labor and futility of the foolish physicians on which we are firm."
"But in that one which is not penetrating and not ancient, cure with iron can be hoped for according to what I will recommend to you, and what I have already said and proved."
"And it is that the disease runs between your buttocks and above your two thighs, raising their folds inside them; the vulva being inclined towards its belly; and then insert a probe of lead or brass if there is turning in the fistula, until you know where the probe passes."
"And if that disease feels around the anus, then it is necessary for you to insert your finger inside the anus."
"And if you feel the probe already entering penetratingly with your finger inserted inside the anus, other than what you feel between your finger and that opening or flesh, then know certainly that it is penetrating; and therefore do not work on it, because there is no cure for it, as we have said."
"But however some say that it is cured in some men."
"And about the treatment by which help is hoped for in this, it is that you ignite a cautery probe according to the width of the fistula, as it is precedented, and insert that burning probe into the fistula until it reaches around the anus; and then repeat it twice or thrice until you know that all those flesh tissues that are fitted together like chicken feather quills are already burnt."
"And then cure it with hot compresses wrapped in linen until all those burnt flesh tissues are softened; and then cure it with medicines that generate and consolidate flesh; and if it is healed, good; but if not, then it will never be healed by any other treatment."
"And if the probe enters but does not penetrate within your finger which is inside the anus, and between that finger and the probe which is covered with skin or flesh tissue, and the fistula seems to be closed at its surface; then cut the skin of the beginning of the fistula, and you will see it cut with the probe, and it should enter into the fistula until the cut reaches the place where the end of the probe arrives, and by the probe it is freed and healed."
"Then cleanse those fleshy fistulas which resemble a bird feather quill, leaving none unaddressed."
"If blood often flows between you and your operation when incising those flesh parts, then it is better to cauterize with fire or sharp medicine, for cautery with fire has two good habits: it adjusts the flesh and dries up the blood and excess humidity."
"And also cure those wounds wrapped in a border or treacherously hidden where the arm meets the body, and also sometimes cure hard gangrenous flesh that generates and solidifies plague."
"And such medicines are styptic and drying; when the wound is restored, it is healed and fears no recurrence."
"But if the fistula has already entered into the anus and is elongated from its surface, then insert your thumb into the anus and search with it."
"And then if you find the bowel and there is a veil of skin or flesh between it and you, it is appropriate to attempt penetration, but this is not an operation performed through an incision, but rather through trust and hope."
"And this is accomplished in one of three ways: either cauterize it as we have said; or cut it so that the concavity of the bowel can be achieved such that you are able to insert some dressings and promote healing; do not proceed with an incision so that you do not wound the lacertum containing the anus, which would accidentally cause injury to the intestines without consent. And also cure it with water as we have said because it will heal quickly; or elongates that veil and clean out that pus by cutting into the bowel properly from behind, as we have said, either with a tent or another sharp instrument, and then cure those fistulated flesh parts which are in the section through cauterization. And also strive to perform the entire operation with an incision, if the opening above is not consolidated, and the fistula remains open at the junction of the anus, it will be easier for healing." "And thus the fistula is finished in this manner: when you insert the tent into the fistula and it is on the side of the anus around its surface with the cord and at the margin of the anus, then take a tent with a perforated extremity, which is like a needle for preparing hearts in this form:"
"And insert the tent into that file wrapped with fine threads or around those [threads]; and then insert the tent with the file into the fistula until it achieves its concavity."
"But if it is penetrating at the margin of the anus from behind, then you remove the thread from that track so that you can insert your finger into the anus; and remove the extremity of the thread and tie the two ends together with a knot, and leave it for one day or two. And when you notice that the thread is becoming embedded in the flesh, cut it there where those flesh parts are incised which are between the two ends of the thread."
"And also cure the wound until it is consolidated and healed."
"But if the opening of the fistula is not penetrating, then make it penetrate in whatever manner you are prepared, but take care that it does not penetrate too far into the front, so that you do not wound the anal sphincter muscle. And then cure it until it is healed."
"The shape of the spatula with spines used to probe the fistula is thus: its curvature is very sharp while the other end is not sharp, so that you do not wound what is not necessary, as sometimes happens."
"Regarding the suturing of hemorrhoids in which blood flows through the incision of those [hemorrhoids]."
"Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: for some are between the buttocks resembling coal, while others are fatty like the fat of bacon." "And among those some are small and large; and blood flows from them constantly, they are many in number, and they are outside the anus, at its extremities."
"But those hemorrhoids that are outside the anus are due to little moisture, from which flows citrine water or a small amount of blood continuously, and they are classified according to the color of the body."
"And the treatment for that which is inside the anus is that you command the patient to sit and express until the anus prolapses and the hemorrhoids appear to you." "Then you grasp with forceps or with your fingers those that have prolapsed and cut them at their roots."
"But if the forceps do not hold those [hemorrhoids] due to their humidity and softness, then grasp them with rough cloth or with cotton or with a wool wisp, and remove them with your fingers. And cut them at their roots and sprinkle some powdered myrrh on that incision so that they are cauterized instead of cauterization; or cauterize them according to what is described in the chapter on cauterization." "And then cure those with another treatment until they are healed."
"And if the anus does not obey to evacuation, then use a clyster on the patient with a small mouthpiece that has been washed with water from the anus and which facilitates evacuation when the patient strains."
"But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then their cause is slight. And you grasp them with your nail or with forceps and cut them. And then cure them with what has been said until they are healed."
"And if you have made an incision, it is necessary that you administer a suture of those [hemorrhoids] as follows: take thread wrapped and insert it into the needle. And remove the hemorrhoids at their roots above, and make the needle penetrate into the root of the other part. And wrap both extremities of the thread in the party below the needle laterally. And tie the hemorrhoid with a tight knot, and then cut the thread and remove the needle."
"And do this to all of them, leaving one intact without tying it, so that the superfluous blood flows from that [hemorrhoid]."
"And then apply over the anus a cloth dipped in rose oil or wax, and have the patient remain lying on their back and command them to retain it." "And then leave that one until it protrudes. And when it has prolapsed, cure it with an ointment or with another treatment until it is healed."
"And if these are very old and cannot be cured by that medicine, then you must remove those with the point of a spatula or your fingernail until they are moistened and scrape off the yellowish pus on top which prevents them from solidifying; and carefully cleanse them so that they may become solid."
"Then take away those with great violence until the first blood comes out and they are scraped; and carefully cleanse them so that they may be healed."
"Know that leprosy is a key disease and it is not if not redondos according to the color of the body like a head of a nail, and it happens throughout the body but more especially in the parts below the elbows and knees, where pain often occurs."
"And then it is necessary that this is incised where the key is located, and removed with forceps or tweezers, and eradicated from its root; and carefully cleanse it."
"If you want to, cauterize the second one that comes next in its chapter."
"But a verruca is a small rough fistulous elevation on the surface of the body and many are often seen in children."
"And its treatment is that you stretch it out and incise it, or scrape it with a file or razor within so that it falls off." "And if you want to, cauterize it as we have said with fire or with an acute medicine."
"But a formica is a small felted or fistulous elevation on the surface of the body, occurring frequently in the forehead, and when it is scratched it feels like the bite of an ant, and it becomes red around the body."
"And its treatment is that you take a quill of an owl or eagle feather, and it should be hard, and place it on the ant so that it contains it within the circle of the quill; and carefully turn your hand with the quill so that you incise what is around the ant, and press it onto the skin of the forehead, and eradicate the ant from its root."
"And if you want to, do this with a needle made of brass or iron according to this method:"
"Let the point of the needle be subtle, blunt (so that it is not perforated), wrapped with a thread so that when you press on it, its revolution becomes easy."
"And if you want to, cauterize the ant according to what is mentioned earlier in the chapter of cautery under the heading of cauterizing a carbuncle."
"Regarding the shapes of instruments that are used for giving cautery."
"Some cautery irons are made of silver or brass or molten lead or hammered ones, and some are made in small and large sizes according to those that they are used for, because the one used for treating young children should be small; and those whose handles are twisted or rounded, their cautery irons should be small."
"The shape of a large cautery iron with few points:"
"The head of the needle at its tip where the bag is tied should be wide in this manner, and it should have such distinction that when the bag is tied, it remains like this."
"And the lower extremity of it, which is inserted into the buttocks, should be blunt (so that it is not open) rather than pointed to subtlety; and on one side there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole, and the width of the holes should correspond to the thickness of the rays or hairs, one large and one small."
"And let the bag in which medicines made from bladder of a beast or wool of sheep are placed have a root that is one hand's breadth."
"And let it be pierced with many holes as it revolves, and if the space between the holes is equal to the thickness of the finger."
"And then insert into those holes a strong thread of raw flax which is made from ten threads, or wind it around them; and adjust the bag with that; and when you have placed the bag on it, let it be tight at the head of the cautery iron between two distinctions with firm constriction, and then cauterize each hole: But the quality of cauterizing in this manner is that you fill the bag with medicine, which should be warmed according to the quantity of the tolerance of the illness; and take care that it is not too cold nor too hot."
"And then let the patient lie on his back, elevate his hips up and place under him either a sheet or a blanket. And then anoint the extremity of the cautery iron with oil or egg white or fenugreek mucilage or something similar; and then insert it into the buttocks gently; and then the assistant takes the bag and squeezes it twice hard so that everything inside the cautery is evacuated from the bowel; and then remove the cautery iron, and let the patient lower his hips to the bed."
"And if the medicine forces him to excrementation, let him retain it as much as possible; and if he sleeps with that throughout one night, it is better for healing."
"But if you cauterize him in cases of diarrhea and loose bowels and excrementation comes out from there, then repeat the cautery until he is healed."
"And if in the buttocks there are hemorrhoids or painful fistulas, then let the cautery iron be very subtle and pointed, those with which children are cauterized."
"Regarding the treatment of plagues."
"I have already stated in the division of the treatment of plagues that which was appropriate for this book, and I now state the treatment of those with medicine according to their completeness."
"I say that plagues are differentiated according to what they are made from, and according to the place where the plague occurs."
"And the causes why many times plagues are made are such as: wounding by a stone, or incision with scissors or knife, or percussion with lance, or club, or arrow, or something similar to those of many causes."
"But the plagues that are in the places of the body are such as: plague which falls on the head, or neck, or foot, or belly, or thigh, and similar to those of the limbs."
"And I am recounting the treatment of some plagues because this reasoning and rule apply to other plagues as well."
"And I will begin with simple head plagues, for the memory of the compound ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter."
"So I say that when a simple head plague occurs and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it is from wounding by a stone or something similar, and the chain has already broken only on this side and the plague is large, and you fear that an abscess will form there, then immediately perform cephalic phlebotomy and do not delay; and extract blood from him according to the quantity of its virtue if no other cause prohibiting phlebotomy exists, especially if the blood that comes out from the plague is little."
"And let the phlebotomy be on the opposite side of the wounded part, and keep the patient from getting drunk and from wine and from heavy foods."
"But if you prohibit some cause because of its minuteness, then let the food be diminished and do not approach meat or wine."
"Place your hand on the wound; if it happens to be cauterized, apply olive oil usually heated or wine in which it has been steeped."
"If you are sure that the wound is cauterized, then place your hand on it; if it is fresh apply the patient's blood and the air has not changed what was put on the powder which I will recommend to you in a moment."
"And if the air has already changed it, then place your hand over the wound until it is healed."
"But if the wound is large or caused by an incision and its lips are not properly adjusted, then adjust those with stitches according to what I will recommend about the stitching of them."
"But if the wound is already exposed to the bone and does not involve retention of it but only a small suspension, then cut that and cure the wound with medicines and restore the flesh properly in place of sinew. Command the patient to be fed on foods which are coarse: heads of cabbage and turnips and things like them until they are convalescent."
"And if you find putrefaction in the sinew and it does not adhere to the bone, then cut away all that is rotten and cast it out, and cure it."
"But if in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flows and it is not severed by medicines, then inquire about the artery. And if you find that it is not cut, then cut it with a scalpel or ligate it. And if necessity requires that what has been said does not help, then cauterize until the bleeding is stopped."
"And if these wounds are simple and small, then the cause of them is light. Therefore you should powder those with this powder, so that it may consolidate them before the air changes them."
"And the manner of making the powder is this: Take oil of sesame one part, dragon's blood two parts, unburnt sulfur three parts. Let all be well ground and sifted, and let the wound be filled with it, and let it be pressed on by good pressure until it adheres to it, and let it be coagulated with the blood."
"And properly press that upon it with powders and leave it alone. Do not remove it while it is like this until it is completely adherent, for the medicine will not abandon it until it is healed."
"And sometimes one does only cauterization when oil of sesame and dragon's blood are not at hand."
"And this is the same operation performed on large wounds when it is necessary to press upon them and bind them tightly, especially fresh wounds with their blood still flowing, which the air has not yet altered."
"But if the air has altered them, especially in summer time, then it is not suitable to use this powder. But at such times treat those wounds with what has been said, thus: you should apply upon them some of these ointments digested, or you should apply upon them flour of barley mixed with water and honey until they are freed from putrefaction; and properly cure them with the other treatment until they are healed."
"But if a fracture of the bone occurs in the wound and it is small, then treat it with this."
"And I direct you to the treatment of fractures of the head in that which follows."
"Of wounds on the neck."
"But if a wound occurs on the neck, there is no difference in treatment between that and a simple wound of the head."
"But if the nerve of the neck is cut or an artery, then if it is a nerve, there is no other remedy but to avoid carelessly treating it with something that causes violent astringency, such as vitriol and similar things which burn nerves and cause contraction." "And do not apply any hot cause upon the wound, for the substance of nerves is hot and their continuity is with the brain, which is the first part of all members."
"And if it is treated with mild medicines such as washing the wound with sweet water, sometimes infused in rose oil or not, and aloe when washed with sweet water and other soft minerals according to this manner, and humid ointments."
"But if the wound is large, then perform suturing or bind its lips together and properly treat it with powders until it is healed."
"But if the wound has depth or occurs in the lower part of the belly with putrefaction, then perforate it in the least depressed place."
"But if an artery has been cut in the wound and bleeding occurs, then separate it or bind it off, ligature it, or cauterize it if necessary."
"But if the spinal cord has been injured or completely severed and the veins of the neck are preserved, then approximate the lips of the wound over the spinal canal with sutures without touching it; afterward extend it evenly and reduce it to its natural shape. Then properly stretch it with decent bandages and leave it alone for a few days. And properly treat it with ointments that have astringency and excitation until it is healed."
"But if the wound has reached the bone and penetrated it deeply, then curette it, and afterward remove all fragments of bone that you can. And what you cannot remove, leave it alone until the wound putrefies and separates itself, and its inflammation is alleviated."
"And if the wound is fresh, then powder it with that powder which I have recommended to you." "But if there is a deep fistula in the wound, then treat it with that of which the memory will come later in its proper chapter."
"If it is a wound from a lance or knife and its depth is uncertain, then consider whether there is wind in the wound when the sick person exhales. If so, know that the wound is mortal."
"And if it is not deep and the wound is fresh with its own blood, then apply to it in the first hour that powder which I have recommended to you. And do not compress it so that the blood is not retained in its depth and returned to the heart, which would aggravate the illness, but rather apply an attractive ointment twice a day."
"And if the ointment is not available, then apply a cotton wick moistened with honey around the wound so that it may suck up its moisture. And make sure that the sick person sleeps on the side of the wound so that what is fitted in it runs."
"But if three days or more have passed since the wound and there has been no spasm or trembling of the heart nor constriction of the lungs and other good dispositions of the sick person occur, then know that the wound is saved. And then treat it with dressings and the other treatment until it is healed."
"But if its healing is delayed and much time has passed, then know that a fistula has formed. Therefore treat it according to the chapter concerning fistulas."
"And if the wound is from a cleaver or knife and is simple on the surface of the foot or back, then treat it with what has been preceded about suture if it is large, or with powder if it is small."
"But if there has already been injury to the bone and pieces of it have already grown into the wound, then turn the wound over and try to remove those pieces if they are detached." If they are not separated, then leave them inside until the plague can improve, for their extraction is alleviated.
And for other accidental plagues in other members, the remedy in treatment is the remedy that we have said.
Of the plagues of the belly.
The indigestion which occurs in the belly is either great, small, or moderate.
And small disruption is done more difficulty by another manner, and therefore the reduction of it is more difficult if you do not promptly introduce them to their proper place, for they are open and enlarged so that the introduction of them is made difficult.
And therefore the best disruption is moderate, for in that one it is not difficult to reduce the belly, as it is in the two species mentioned above.
And know that there are four ways of suturing the belly, but two of them are common and suitable for sutures of other plagues of the body.
And two others are proper to other plagues, but especially proper in suturing the belly.
And I will recount to you each one with exposition and explanation.
Therefore I say that when the plague is small and some cause of the belly is exited by it, and it is difficult to reduce it, then this is in one of two ways: either by the smallness of the disruption as we have said, or when the belly has become inflated by the coldness of the air.
And therefore when it is thus, then you should scalp that in such a way that you submerge a sponge or wet cloth in water alone or squeeze in hot water cumin, parsley, and broth with that the inflation may be resolved.
And sometimes you will find it useful to use wine in which there is astringency, and it is better than water alone in the resolution of inflammation.
And therefore when you see that the inflammation is resolved, then you should moisten the belly with water in which is cooked mallow and mallows, for by this it is alleviated from within with little cause.
But if the intrusion of the belly has been removed by this remedy, then you should cut through the disruption a little with an instrument with which you can excise the hemorrhoids.
And the first remedy is better when it is suitable that it not be cut and there is no need to cut unnecessarily or rashly.
About the instrument, see its shape:
The one part of it is cut sharp and the other not-sharp, and the extremity is subtle, but not as subtle as a spatula, rather let it be somewhat obtuse.
And therefore when the plague is enlarged and goes out from the belly, then it is necessary that its reduction be according to its natural form in its own proper place, if this is possible about this, for this is better.
But when the disruption is wide and is in the lower part of the belly, then you should make the sick person lie on their back and raise their buttocks as high as their head; and if it is in the upper part of the belly, then you should raise the head of the bed and place the feet higher than the shoulders.
And similarly if the disruption is in one of the two parts of the belly, then always keep your intention and consideration on this so that the part in which the plague is may be higher than the other.
And thus you should administer this in large plagues and medium-sized ones.
And in small plagues, keep this that is prepared by you and especially make sure that the person administering it is among your closest friends, who should hold the disruption entirely with their hand and adjust the lips of it, and especially uncover from here to there so that no stitching occurs unnecessarily.
And this is the common manner of suturing: you take a needle or count of needles according to the quantity of the breadth of the plague; and then lay aside from the extremity of the disruption the finger of the ring finger, and stretch the needle once, but do not put thread in both extremities of the cord with two extremities of the ciphac that is left behind the cords of the fingers inside, until you make it penetrate this part; and you have now added two extremities of the cord and two extremities of the ciphac, and so you have made four orders.
And then stretch with doubled thread around the needle, and sometimes from two parts together, and then join both lips and the plague by a decent joining; and then leave the thickness of the finger and put another needle in that, and then join this with thread thus like feast with the first needle; and do not cease doing this if it is necessary with needles until you have completed all the contraction of the plague.
And let the needles be medium in thickness and subtlety, for thin needles easily cut the flesh; and thick ones are difficult to put into the cord, therefore they should be medium in thickness and subtlety.
And it is not necessary that the needle be put in both extremities of the cord very much, lest the flesh be easily cut and the plague open before its consolidation.
And do not prolong the suturing so that the plague is not prohibited from consolidation.
And then cut the extremities of the needles so that they do not disturb the sick person during their sleep; and you will sprinkle powder on the suturing from every part, which holds the extremities of the needles; and leave them until you know that the plague is already consolidated.
And these kinds of suturing with needles in what manner are more convenient for small plagues, for there is enough in the suturing of them with one needle or two or around those.
But the second kind of suturing is common: it is that you administer with suturing the four extremities, of the cord and two extremities of the ciphac, in one go, with a needle on which there is thread wrapped around it subtly and thickly.
And then when the needle has penetrated these four extremities, reduce the needle from that same part where you began, so that the thread draws back and goes from the lower part of the plague to the higher one, so that the suturing is according to the sewing of cloth with which the cloths are stretched.
And pause between each suturing the quantity of the thickness of the little finger.
And this kind of suturing is known by men.
And with such suturing I healed the plague that had been cut in a man's belly, which had been struck with a dagger, and the disruption of the plague was more than a palm wide, and it had issued from the bowels around two palms of the bowel of the middle place, and the disruption was in the middle of the member; and then I reduced that after the bowel had been forced by the plague for twenty-four hours.
And the plague was consolidated in the space of fifteen days or around, and he was cured and is healthy; and thus he lived for many years, and is converted in his dispositions.
And the other doctors had judged that he would not be healed; and by miracle it was done, for I did not cure him with ointment, because there was a place where ointment was not found nor any medicine, but only paused over the plague twice a day and washed it diligently with water of honey until it was healed.

"But judgment about the treatment of pleurisy is also judgment about other kinds of pleurisy."

"Of the treatment of furuncles and fistulas."
"Do you know that any ulcer or abscess which opens and becomes chronic without being consolidated and drained always, wherever it may be in the body, is called a fistula, and we call this type of boil an 'azukem'?"
"And in truth, a fistula is a hard, thick, white node without pain and with a concavity like the concavity of a chicken's egg; for this reason it is called a 'rizat' ulcer, that is to say, an egg."
"And in some people it is moist, which oozes out; but if the moisture is quickly drained off, it heals in a few days." "Sometimes this moisture is abundant, thick, and subtle."

Of leg vein extraction
This vein is generated in the calves of the legs, such as at Atig in Arab territory and in dry and hard terrains of little tenderness where there is neither grass nor water.
And it is also generated in other places on the body apart from the calves.
And its gestation is of putrefaction which comes from leaving the spine like venom inside the body, serpents and worms, crabs and worms generating between the spine and the flesh.
And the sign of the onset of its occurrence is that this vein becomes inflamed in the calf with a sudden inflammation; and nearby there is an ulceration; and from there begins the vein to come out from that ulceration which appears like the root of a plant.
And then when the extremity appears, immediately you must wrap around it one weight of lead whose weight is that of one dragon, between two dragons, and hold it there and let the lead hang suspended from the calf.
And as many times as some cause causes it to come out from its places outside, wrap that in lead and hold it there. And if it is not prolonged, then you should cut off a part of it and wrap up the remaining; but do not cut it so deep that it remains inside, for if you cut it too deeply it will contract and enter into the flesh and cause an aposteme and putrefaction in the place with a bad ulceration.
For that reason it should be treated gently and extracted little by little until it is completely removed from the end of it and none remains inside the body.
And this vein has been found in some men to be as long as two palms and ten fingers, and I have even heard that one was twenty palms long.
And if it is cut at the time of its treatment, then insert a straw into the track of it and pierce it with a long straw through the body until all that is in the matter has been evacuated, and administer putrefaction to the place for some days with medicines; and also treat it with the cure for apostemes.
And this vein sometimes has many branches, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot or in the foot, and comes out from there with many openings, and each opening has its own branch.
And therefore treat it as we have said in the division above, and with what is said above.
Of cutting for worms generated under the skin, called bovine ailment.
This ailment is called in some lands "bovine ailment" because many times it occurs in oxen, and there is born between the skin and the flesh a worm which goes throughout the body, pushing and pulling, and is felt from member to member until it tears apart the skin and comes out.
And its generation occurs because of putrefaction of certain humors, just as happens with worms and serpents and earthworms and roundworms in the belly.
And it is feared because of its harmfulness, for when it goes in the body and rises up to the head, and reaches the brain, then it causes a great disturbance there and enters and destroys the brain, which happens many times.
And therefore when you wish to cure it and extract it, then do not do so unless you see its movement and appearance by feeling it, and then you should press down on what is above it and on both sides of it with pressure and constriction, and then dry up around it and extract it.
And if it is embedded in the flesh and cannot be caught hold of, then you should apply a cautery with fire to the place where it resides until it is burnt up, for the greatest danger is corruption of it with which it corrupts the place as we have said.
But if it reaches the head near the brain, then press strongly on the brow with firm constriction and also dry up around it and extract it; and let the patient use medicines to purge his body of bad corrupt humors, and avoid foods that cause putrefaction.
Of cutting for the ailment called nafir
This ailment is called in our land "nafir," and it is a pain that comes in some members, and also changes from member to member.
And you will see this one as I will describe to you. I was called to see a woman patient in a village, and I uncovered her arm and saw a small inflammation in the vein of the elbow, and as it had been there for about an hour, I saw that inflammation move like a worm pushing itself along, but more slowly than if it were actually moving, just as if it were molten silver running from place to place.
And then the pain went away from that place and became apparent in the muscle, and stayed there for about an hour.
"Next, correct the other body between where it reaches the other arm."
"I also told him to turn himself around so that I could see his whole body; and he was amazed at the transformation of his limbs and their speed." "And I had seen such things before in my travels according to that manner, but I had never heard of anyone suffering pain from being transformed limb by limb." "But I did not see this among the women as I saw it in men."
"And you do not think that is because the woman was old, with dry skin and visible veins, and in this appearance there seemed to be that windiness transformed."
"And it is necessary that this backward curvature does not appear in those who are graceful and have moist skin with veins concealed."

"But if you do not see it among your patients, then treat him with exercise of the body and with what expels windiness, and apply to him pills made from fetid herbs and pills made from serpentaria and similar things."
"On the extraction of arrows."
Arrows are diverse according to species and the parts of the body where they strike, for their diversity is such that those with large points, small ones, concave tips, or blunt heads are solid; while those with three edges, tongues, or star-shaped tips have different properties.
"Servants are distinguished by when an arrow strikes them and passes through the bone, exiting from the cyphac which is on the brain. This occurs due to violent soda and scotomia, vertigo, redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, vomiting bile, speech is suddenly cut off, voice destroyed, and white humid plague-like matter exits from the place, similar to water."
"If these symptoms appear before you, then you should abstain from treatment and extraction of the arrow if it is not outside."
"When the arrow strikes near the left breast and seems to be stuck in hard flesh, not soft flesh, you will feel a sudden movement like a pulse or flow of black blood. There will also be coldness in the extremities, chills, sweating, fainting, and soon after death without delay."
"And when the arrow has pierced the lung, there is an emission of frothy blood from the wound. The vessels near the neck swell up, the patient's complexion changes, they expire loudly or sigh for breath frequently, and desire cool air."
"And if the arrow strikes the diaphragm, which is located in the lower chest area, there will be pain near the lower ribs. There will also be sudden, violent coughing with pain and sighs, but not all members or muscles will be affected."
"And if the arrow strikes the stomach, then there will be violent vomiting of undigested food."
"And if the arrow strikes the abdomen and becomes lodged within it, then there will be some hole or tear in the skin, flesh, or intestines (which may have ruptured). There is little hope for recovery through extraction of the arrow."
"And if the arrow strikes the bladder and urine is excreted externally, with some blood or other matter from the wound outside. There will be severe pain over the area of injury, indicating that death is imminent."
"However, the other members such as the face, neck, throat, shoulders, arms, spine, collarbone, hip, thigh and their counterparts are saved according to the greatest dispositions when the arrow does not hit any vein or artery, nor is it venomous."
"And I will tell you what I have seen of these arrows, so that you may know about their treatment."
"The cause is that in a man who was struck by an arrow in the lacrimal gland of his eye near the root of his nose, when I extracted it from the other side of his ear, he recovered without any injury to his eye."
"And I extracted another arrow from a Jew who was struck in the eyelid of his eye, leaving the eyelid puffed up afterwards. The arrow was already hidden and could not be seen except for a small part that adhered to its shaft. It was one of the sharp arrows of the Turks with a lion's head made of iron without feathers."
"And the Jew recovered, and there was no great harm done to his eye."
"And I extracted another arrow from a Christian man who was struck in the throat. It was an Arab arrow with feathers on it, and I cut through it between two guides and then carefully extracted it. The Christian man recovered."
"And I extracted another arrow from a man who was struck in his belly and thought that he would die from it. "And I saw a woman who was struck by an arrow in her belly. The wound healed over inside her without any change in her condition, and the woman suffered no injury to any of her natural functions."
"And I saw another man who was struck by an arrow in his face. The wound healed over and the arrow head broke off without causing much pain, and he appeared similar to these others."
"And I extracted the arrow from the face of one of the king's nobles that was lodged in his nasal septum and had deviated slightly towards the right side. The entire arrow was hidden."
